\newbox\ncintdbox \newbox\ncinttbox %% noncommutative integral symbols
\setbox0=\hbox{$-$} \setbox2=\hbox{$\displaystyle\int$}
\setbox\ncintdbox=\hbox{\rlap{\hbox
		to \wd2{\hskip-.125em \box2\relax\hfil}}\box0\kern.1em}
\setbox0=\hbox{$\vcenter{\hrule width 4pt}$}
\setbox2=\hbox{$\textstyle\int$} \setbox\ncinttbox=\hbox{\rlap{\hbox
		to \wd2{\hskip-.175em \box2\relax\hfil}}\box0\kern.1em}

		{\copy\ncinttbox}{\copy\ncinttbox}%
		{\copy\ncinttbox}}\nolimits}  %% NC integral

	\newbox\ncintdbox \newbox\ncinttbox %% noncommutative integral symbols
	\setbox0=\hbox{$-$}
	\setbox2=\hbox{$\displaystyle\int$}
	\setbox\ncintdbox=\hbox{\rlap{\hbox
			to \wd2{\box2\relax\hfil}}\box0\kern.1em}
	\setbox0=\hbox{$\vcenter{\hrule width 4pt}$}
	\setbox2=\hbox{$\textstyle\int$}
	\setbox\ncinttbox=\hbox{\rlap{\hbox
			to \wd2{\hskip-.05em\box2\relax\hfil}}\box0\kern.1em}

	\newcommand{\snorm}[1]{\mathopen{\tribar}{#1}%
		\mathclose{\tribar}}                 %% norm |||x|||

	\title{Algebraic topology of $C^*$-algebras}
	
	\author
	{\textbf{Petr R. Ivankov* 10.02   13:50}\\
		e-mail: * monster.ivankov@gmail.com \\
	}
	
	
	\begin{document}
\maketitle  %\setlength{\parindent}{0pt}
\pagestyle{plain}

\begin{abstract}
	\noindent
\paragraph{}	Any $C^*$-algebra can be regarded as a generalization of locally compact Hausdorff topological space $\mathcal X$. Here we consider a generalization of fundamental group and (co)homology theory. In result one has invariants  of $C^*$-algebras such that: 
	\begin{itemize}
		\item for any commutative $C^*$-algebra $A = C_0\left(\sX \right)$ the invariants of $A$ coincide with the  $\sX$ ones,
		\item the theory is not trivial even for algebras having bad spectrum, e.g. containing  one point only.
	\end{itemize}
	Instead of $\sX$ we consider the space $\sY$ which should not be Hausdorff. However a noncommutative $C^*$-algebra $A$ defines $\sY$ and sometimes vice-versa.
	
\end{abstract}
\section{General Theory}
\subsection{The Gelfand space of $C^*$-algebra}

\begin{definition}\label{lattice_a_defn}
If $A$ be a $C^*$-algebra then $A$-\textit{semi}-\textit{lattice} is the meet-semilattice (cf. Definition \ref{lattice_defn}) of closed left ideals such that 
\be\label{meet_eqn}
\begin{split}
L' \wedge L''\bydef L' \cap L'',\\
L' \le L'' \quad \Leftrightarrow\quad L' \subset L'',\\
0 \bydef \{0\}\subset A.
\end{split}
\ee
A filter (resp, an ultrafilter) of $A$-lattice is an $A$-\textit{filter} (resp. an $A$-\textit{ultrafilter}) (cf. Definitions \ref{filter_defn} and \ref{ultra_filter_defn}).
We denote this semilattice by $\mathfrak{Lattice}\left( A\right)$. Denote by $\mathfrak{Filters}\left( A\right)$  (resp.  $\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left( A\right)$) the  set of $A$-filters  (resp. $A$-ultrafilters).
\end{definition}
\begin{lemma}\label{top_lattices_iso_lem}
	For any locally compact space $\sX$ there is an isomorphism of  meet-semilattices
 
\be
\begin{split}
	\mathfrak{Lattice}_\sX : \mathfrak{Lattice}\left( C_0\left(  \sX\right)\right)\cong \mathfrak{Lattice}\left(\sX \right).
%	L \mapsto\sX \setminus \left\{x \in \sX | \forall a \in L \quad a(x) = 0\right\}.
\end{split}
\ee	
where  $\mathfrak{Lattice}\left(\sX \right)$ is the lattice of open subsets of $\sX$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
Any left ideal of  $C_0\left(  \sX\right)$ is a two-sided ideal. This lemma can be deduced from the proof of the Theorem \ref{gelfand-naimark_thm}.
\end{proof}
\begin{empt}\label{topology_empt}
 If $\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)$ 
  is a set of $A$-ultrafilters (cf. Definition \ref{lattice_a_defn}) of the meet-semilattice $\mathfrak{Lattice}\left( A\right)$  then there is a topology on $\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)$ is the minimal among topologies such that for any closed left ideal $L \subset A$ the set
 
	\be\label{topology_eqn}
\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)_L	\bydef \left\{\left. \xi \in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right) \right| \exists L' \in \xi\quad L'\cap L = \{0\} \right\}
	\ee
 set is open.
	
\end{empt}
\begin{definition}\label{gelfand_space_defn}
	If $A$ is a $C^*$-algebra then	an ultrafilter  $\xi \in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)$ is an $A$-\textit{finite point} if there is a nontrivial element $a\in K\left( A\right)\setminus\{0\}$ such that 
	$$
	Aa \in \xi.
	$$
	The \textit{Gelfand space} $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$ of $C^*$-algebra $A$ is a space  of finite points with the final topology (cf. Definition \ref{top_final_defn}) given by the natural inclusion $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right) \hookto \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)$.
\end{definition}
\begin{remark}
	The given by  	\eqref{topology_eqn} sets yield a subbase (cf. Definition \ref{top_subbase_defn})  of the topology of the Gelfand space  $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$. The base (cf. Definition \ref{top_base_defn}) of $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$ is given by the sets
		\be\label{topology_base_eqn}
 \left\{ \xi \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right) \left| \exists L \in \xi\quad L\cap \left( \bigcup_{j=1}^n L_j\right)  = \{0\}\right. \right\}
	\ee
	where $L_1,..., L_n$ are closed left ideals.
\end{remark}


\begin{definition}\label{open_ideal_defn}
	If $L_1,..., L_n\subset A$ are closed left ideals and
	\bean
	\sU \bydef \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right) \bigcap \left(  \bigcap_{j = 1}^n \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)_{L_j}\right) \subset \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A\right)
	\eean 
	is an element of basis (cf. Definition \ref{top_base_defn}) then the closure of the union
	\bean
	\bigcup \left\{ L \text{ is a left ideal of } A  \left| L \bigcap  \left( \bigcup_{j= 1}^n L_j \right) = \{0\}\right.\right\}
		\eean 
		is the  $\sU$-\textit{space}
		If $\sU \bydef \bigcup_\iota \sU_\iota$ is any union of belonging to a basis open subsets $\sU_\iota$ then the $\sU$-\textit{space} is the closure of $L_{\sU_\iota}$ where  $L_{\sU_\iota}$ is the $\sU_\iota$
		
\end{definition}

\begin{empt}\label{topology_base_herd_empt}
	Using the Lemma \ref{hered_ideal_lem} one can replace the closed left ideals in the Definition \ref{gelfand_space_defn} with right ones or hereditary $C^*$-subalgebras. For any filter $\xi$ we use a following notation
	\be\label{hered_ideal_eqn}
	L \in \xi \quad \Leftrightarrow \quad B \bydef L \cap L^* \in \xi\quad \Leftrightarrow \quad L^* \in \xi.
	\ee
	So the Gelfand space can be be regarded as a subset of ultrafilters of right ideals and/or a set of ultrafilters of hereditary $C^*$ subalgebras of $B \subset A$ such that there is $a \in \K\left( A\right)_+$ with
	\be
	B \subset a A a
	\ee
	Similarly to \eqref{topology_base_eqn} the base (cf. Definition \ref{top_base_defn}) of $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$ is given by the sets
			\be\label{topology_base_herd_eqn}
	\left\{ \xi \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right) \left| \exists B \in \xi\quad B\cap \left( \bigcup_{j=1}^n B_j\right)  = \{0\}\right. \right\}
	\ee
	where $B$,  $B_1,..., B_n$ are hereditary $C^*$ subalgebras of $A$.
	
\end{empt}

The following Lemma is a generalization of the Theorem \ref{gelfand-naimark_thm}.
\begin{lemma}\label{lem_g_lem} (Generalized commutative Gelfand theorem).
	If $\sX$ is a locally compact, Hausdorff space then  is a natural  homeomorphism $ \mathfrak{Gelfand}_\sX: \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(C_0\left( \sX\right) \right)\cong \sX$, where  $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(C_0\left( \sX\right)\right)$ is the Gelfand space.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
	
	From the Lemma \ref{top_lattices_iso_lem}  it turns out that for any locally compact space $\sX$ there is an isomorphism of  meet-semilattices
	
	\bean
	\begin{split}
		\mathfrak{Lattice}_\sX : \mathfrak{Lattice}\left( C_0\left(  \sX\right)\right)\cong \mathfrak{Lattice}\left(\sX \right).
		%	I \mapsto\sX \setminus \left\{x \in \sX | \forall a \in I \quad a(x) = 0\right\}.
	\end{split}
	\eean  
	It follows that there is a homeomorphism 
	$$
\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}_\sX : \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left( C_0\left(  \sX\right)\right)\cong \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\sX \right)
	$$ 	
	of spaces of ultrafilters. If $\xi \in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left( C_0\left(  \sX\right)\right)$ then  denote by 
	$$
\sV_\xi\bydef 	\bigcap_{\sU \in \xi }\sU
	$$
	
	If $x \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( C_0\left(  \sX\right)\right)$ then there if $a \in K\left( C_0\left( \sX\right) \right) \cong C_c\left( \sX\right)$ such that
	$$
aA \in \xi
	$$
or equivalently $\sV_\xi\subset  \supp a$.
	If 
	$$
\xi_a \bydef 	\left\{\left.\sU \cap \supp a \right| \sU \in \xi \right\}\in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left( {\supp a}\right) 
	$$
	then  from the Proposition \ref{top_ultra_thm} it turns out that $\xi_a$ has the unique limit. This limit corresponds to $\mathfrak{Gelfand}_\sX\left( \xi\right)= \mathfrak{Gelfand}_{\supp a}\left( \xi_a\right)$. So we have the map is the set theoretic bijection. From the equation \ref{topology_eqn} one can deduce that the any open subset of $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(C_0\left( \sX\right)\right)$ with  corresponds to an open subset of $\sX$ and vice versa. 
	\end{proof}

\begin{definition}\label{commutant_defn}
	Let $A$ be a $C^*$-algebra and let $L$ be a closed left ideal. The closed left ideal
	$$
	L^\perp \bydef \bigcup \left\{a \in A | L a^* = \{{0}\} \right\}
	$$
	is the \textit{commutant} of $L$ (write $L^\perp$).;
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}\label{bicommutant_defn}
For any element $\xi \in  \mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(A \right)$ the \textit{bicommutant} of $\xi$ (written $\xi^{\perp\perp}$ or $\xi''$) is the closure of the union
$$
\bigcup_{L \in \xi} L^\perp.
$$
If for any $\xi\in \mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(A \right)$ the bicommutant $\xi''$  is the proper left ideal 
then the set of bicommutants  (write $\mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(A \right)^{\perp\perp}$ or $\mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(A \right)''$) is the \textit{bicommutant} of $\mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(A \right)$.  Under this hypothesis There is the natural surjective  map 
\be\label{bicommutant_to_eqn}
 \mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(A \right) \xrightarrow{\phi''}  \mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(A \right)''
\ee
We imply that the topology of $\mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(A \right)''$  is final with respect to the map $\phi''$ (cf. Definition \ref{top_final_defn}).
\end{definition}

\begin{example}
From the Lemma \ref{lem_g_lem} it follows that there is a homeomorphism $\mathfrak{Gelfand}_\sX: \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(C_0\left( \sX\right)  \right)\cong \sX$. If $x = \mathfrak{Gelfand}_\sX\left( \xi\right)$ then for any $L \in \xi$ there is an open neighborhood of $x$ such that 
\bean
\forall a \in L \quad a\left(\sX \setminus \sU \right) = \{0\}
\eean  
so one has
\bean
\forall a \in L^\perp \quad a\left(\sU \right) = \{0\}
\eean

If $L_x \bydef \left\{a \in C_0\left(\sX \right) | a\left(x \right)= 0  \right\}$ 
the for any positive   $a'\in L_x$ one has
\be\label{pden_eqn}
\begin{split}
\left\|a' - f_{\eps/2}\left(a' \right)  \right\| < \eps,\\
\exists L \in \xi \quad a' \in L^\perp.\
\end{split}
\ee 
where $f_\eps$ is given by \eqref{f_eps_eqn}. From the equation \eqref{pden_eqn} it turns out that the subset of positive elements of the union $\cup  L^\perp$ is dense  in  the subset of positive elements of $L_x$.
If $A$ is a $C^*$-algebra then one has
\be\label{four_decompositon_eqn}
\forall a \in A\quad \exists a_1, a_2, a_3, a_4 \in A_+\quad a=a_1 - a_2 + ia_3 - ia_4 \quad  a_1, a_2, a_3, a_4 \ge 0.
\ee
From \eqref{four_decompositon_eqn} it follows that the the union $\cup  L^\perp$ is dense in $L_x$, so one has $L_x \subset \xi'' \bydef \phi''\left( \xi\right) $ (cf. Definition \ref{bicommutant_defn}). On the other hand if $a \notin L_x$ then $\left\|a\left(x \right)  \right\| > 0$ and
\bean
\forall L \in \xi \quad \exists a' \in L \quad a'\left(x \right)\neq 0 \quad  \Rightarrow \quad a'\left( x\right) a^*\left( x\right) \neq 0\quad  \Rightarrow \quad a'a^* \neq 0.
\eean 
So one has $\xi'' \subset L_x$, and  $\xi'' = L_x$. From this fact it turns out that the given by \eqref{bicommutant_to_eqn} map is a  homeomorphism from  $\mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(A \right)$ onto $ \mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(A \right)''$.
\end{example}



\begin{definition}\label{belongs_defn}
	Let $A$ be a $C^*$ -algebra and let $\hat A$ be the spectrum of $A$ (cf. Definition \ref{spectrum_prime_primtive_defn}). An element $\xi \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$  \textit{belongs to } $x \in \hat A$ if one has
	\be\label{belongs_eqn}
	\forall L \in \xi \quad \rep_x\left(L\right) \neq \{0\} 
	\ee
	where $\rep_x : A \to B\left(\H_x \right)$ is an irreducible representation (cf. Definition  \ref{irred_defn}).  Similarly the bicommutant $\xi''$ \textit{belongs to} $x$ if $\rep_x\left(\xi'' \right) \neq \rep_x\left(A \right)$.
	
\end{definition}
\begin{empt}
	Under the hypothesis of the Definition \ref{belongs_defn}  if $x', x'' \in \hat A$ with $x' \neq x''$ and $\xi\in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$ belongs to both $x'$, and $x''$ then the generated by the set $\left\{ L \cap \ker_{x'}\right\}$ filter exceeds $\xi$. It is impossible since $\xi$ is an ultrafilter. Moreover
	\be\label{not_bel}
	\begin{split}
		\forall x \in \hat A \quad \xi \text{ does not belong to } x \quad \Rightarrow \quad \exists L  \in \xi \quad \rep_x\left( L\right) = \{0\}.
	\end{split}
	\ee
	
	So there is the natural continuous map:
	\be\label{to_spec_eqn} 
	\begin{split}
\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right) \xrightarrow{\hat \phi} \hat A
	\end{split}
	\ee
Moreover if there is the bicommutant $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)''$ of $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$ (cf. Definition \ref{bicommutant_defn}) then the map $\hat \phi$ naturally induces the continuous map $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)'' \xrightarrow{\hat \phi''} \hat A$ with the following commutative diagram
	\be\label{not_c_bel}
		\begin{tikzcd}
			\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right) \arrow[rr, "\phi''" ]  \arrow[rd, "\hat \phi" ]& & \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)'' \arrow[ld, "\hat \phi''" ]\\
			& \hat A&
\end{tikzcd}
\ee

\end{empt}

%\begin{definition}\label{red_geland_defn}
%Let $A$ be a $C^*$-algebra, and  let both $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A\right$ be its Gelfand space. Consider the equivalence relations 
%\bean
%\forall \xi',\xi''\in\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A\right) \quad   \xi'\sim\xi''\quad \Leftrightarrow \quad\\ \left(
%\forall \text{ open set }\quad  \sU \subset  \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A\right\quad 
%\xi' \in \sU
%\quad \Leftrightarrow \quad \xi'' \in \sU \right).
%\eean 
%The quotient spaces 
%\bean

%\end{definition}
\subsection{Morphisms}
\paragraph*{}
If both $A$ and $\widetilde{A}$ are $C^*$-algebra then any injective  homomorphism 	
\be\label{phi_r_eqn}
\varphi_M: A \hookto M\left(\widetilde A\right)	
\ee
of $\C$-algebras such that
\be\label{closed_p_eqn}
\widetilde{ A }\quad \text{is the closure of} \quad \widetilde A \varphi_M\left( A\right).
\ee
yields an injective homomorphism  
\be\label{lat_mor_eqn}
\begin{split}
	\mathfrak{Lattice}\left(  A\right) \xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Lattice}\left(\varphi_M \right)}\mathfrak{Lattice} \left( \widetilde A\right),\\
	L \mapsto \text{ the closure of } \widetilde A \varphi_M\left(L \right).
	\end{split}
	\ee
	On the other hand the homomorphism $\mathfrak{Lattice}\left(\varphi_M \right)$ yields a mapping of filters
\be\label{fil_mor_eqn}
\begin{split}
	\mathfrak{Filters}\left(  A\right) \xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Filters}\left(\varphi_M \right)}\mathfrak{Filters} \left( \widetilde A\right),\\
	\left\{L_\la\right\}_{\la \in \La} \mapsto \text{ a filter generated by } \bigcup_{\la \in \La} \left\{\mathfrak{Lattice}\left(\varphi_M \right)\left( L_\la\right) \right\}_{\la \in \La}
\end{split}
\ee
If $\xi \in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(  A\right) $ is an ultrafilter then we define a set
\bean
\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\varphi_M \right)^{-1}\left(\xi \right) \bydef\left\{\left.\widetilde \xi \in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\widetilde  A\right)\right|\forall \widetilde{L}'\in \mathfrak{Filters}\left(\varphi_M \right)\left( \xi\right)\subset \widetilde \xi \right\}
\eean
For all $\xi', \xi''\in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)$ with $\xi' \neq \xi''$ there are $L' \in \xi'$ and $L'' \in \xi''$ such that $L'\cap L'' = \{0\}$. It turns out that
\bean
\xi', \xi''\in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)\quad \xi' \neq \xi'' \quad \Rightarrow\\
\Rightarrow \quad \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\varphi_M \right)^{-1}\left(\xi' \right)\cap \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\varphi_M \right)^{-1}\left(\xi ''\right)= \emptyset
\eean 
Using the above map one can construct the natural map
\be\label{ultra_mor_eqn}
\begin{split}
	\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\varphi_M \right)\left( \widetilde \xi\right) = \xi \quad \Leftrightarrow \quad \widetilde \xi \in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\varphi_M \right)^{-1}\left(\xi \right),\\
	\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\widetilde  A\right) \xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\varphi_M \right)}\mathfrak{Ultrafilters} \left( A\right).
\end{split}
\ee


\begin{defn}\label{good_defn}
The injective homomorphism \eqref{lat_mor_eqn} is \textit{good} if the given by \eqref{ultra_mor_eqn} map $\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\varphi_M \right)$ yields the natural   map
	\be\label{gelfand_map_eqn}
\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\widetilde A \right)\xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\varphi_M \right)}\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right).
\ee
\end{defn}
\begin{lemma}\label{good_lem}
If the  homomorphism \eqref{lat_mor_eqn} is good 	  then the map \eqref{gelfand_map_eqn} is continuous.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
	From the equation \eqref{topology_eqn} one can deduce any closed  set of  $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A\right)$  corresponds to a closed set of $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\widetilde A\right)$.
\end{proof}.
\begin{empt}\label{bicommutant_empt}
	Let $\varphi_M: A \hookto M\left(\widetilde A\right)$ be a good morphism. If $\widetilde \xi \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\widetilde A \right)$ and 
  $\widetilde \xi'' \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\widetilde A \right)''$ is the corresponding element  of bicommutant (cf. Definition \ref{bicommutant_defn} then there is $\widetilde{a}\in \widetilde{\xi}''$ end $\eps > 0$ such that
  \be\label{b_neq_eqn}
  \forall a_1, ..., a_n \in \xi'' \quad \forall \widetilde a_1, ..., \widetilde a_n \in A\quad \left\| \sum_{j =1}^n \widetilde a_j a_j - \widetilde a,\right\| > \eps.
  \ee
 where $\xi''$ is the bicommutant of  $\xi = \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\varphi_M \right) \left(\widetilde \xi \right)$. From
 \bean
 \forall L \in \xi \quad \text{the closure of } \widetilde A \varphi_M\left( L\right) \in \widetilde \xi.
 \eean 
it follows that 
 \bean
 \forall L \in \xi \quad \exists \widetilde L \in \widetilde \xi \quad \widetilde A   \varphi\left(L^\perp \right) \subset \widetilde L^\perp.
 \eean 
 If the closure $L'$ of the union 
 $$
 \bigcap_{L \in \xi} L^\perp 
 $$
 is not proper ideal the for any $a \in A$ and $\dl > 0$ there is $a' \in L'$  such that $\left\| a - a' \right\|< \dl$. If  $a'_1, ..., a'_n \in L'$ such that
 \bean
 \left\| a_j - a'_j \right\| < \frac{\eps}{n \left\|\widetilde  a_j  \right\|}
 \eean 
 then
 $$
 \left\| \sum_{j =1}^n \widetilde a_j a_j - \widetilde a,\right\| < \eps
 $$
 Above equation contradicts with \eqref{b_neq_eqn} one.
\end{empt}
\begin{lemma}\label{bicommutant_lem}
Any good morphism $\varphi_M: A \hookto M\left(\widetilde A\right)$ yields a continuous map
\be\label{bicommutant_eqn} 
\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\widetilde A \right)''\xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\varphi_M \right)''}\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)''.
\ee
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
The existence of the map follows from \ref{bicommutant_empt}. The continuity can be deduced from the continuity of $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\varphi_M \right)$.
\end{proof}
\subsection{Coverings and fundamental group}

\begin{definition}\label{connected_c_a_defn}
	We say that a $C^*$-algebra $A$ is \textit{connected} if it cannot be represented as a direct sum  $A \cong A' \oplus A''$ of nontrivial $C^*$-algebras $A'$ and $A''$.
	
	% (the Gelfand spectrum of the center of $M\left( A\right) $ is connected). Let $A \subset B$ be a connected subalgebra. We say that $A$ is a \textit{connected component} of $B$ if  $1_{M\left( A\right) }$ lies in the center of $1_{M\left( B\right) }$.
\end{definition}
\begin{definition}\label{fin_pre_defn}
	Let   $A$ be an unital connected $C^*$-algebra  and let  $\widetilde{A}$ be  connected $C^*$-algebra (cf. Definition \ref{connected_c_a_defn}), and let $\lift: A \hookto M\left( \widetilde{A}\right) $ be an injective  $*$-homomorphism of % connected
	$C^*$-algebras such that following conditions hold:
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item[(a)] $\lift\left( 1_A\right) = 1_{ M\left( \widetilde{A}\right)}$,
		\item[(b)] if $\Aut\left(\widetilde{A} \right)$ is a group of $*$-automorphisms of $\widetilde{A}$ then the group  
		\be\nonumber
		G \bydef \left\{ \left.g \in \Aut\left(\widetilde{A} \right)~\right|\forall a \in \lift \left(M\left(  A\right) \right) \quad ga = a\right\}
		\ee
		is discrete with respect to the described in the Section \ref{op_top_sec} topologies,
		\item[(c)] 	$A = M\left( \widetilde{A}\right) ^G\stackrel{\text{def}}{=}\left\{\left.a\in \widetilde{A}~~\right|\forall g \in G\quad  a = g a\right\}$.
	\end{enumerate}
	We say that the triple $\left(A, \widetilde{A}, G \right)$ and/or the quadruple $\left(A, \widetilde{A}, G, \lift \right)$ and/or $*$-homomorphism $\lift: A \hookto M\left( \widetilde{A}\right) $   is a \textit{noncommutative  pre-covering}. We write $G\left(\left.\widetilde A~\right|A \right)\bydef G$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}\label{evenly_defn}
	
	Let $\left(A, \widetilde{A}, G, \lift \right)$ be a noncommutative  pre-covering (cf. Definition \ref{fin_pre_defn})
	A connected hereditary $C^*$-subalgebra $B \subsetneqq A$ 
	is $\left(A, \widetilde{A}, G, \lift \right)$- \textit{evenly covered by} $\left(A, \widetilde{A}, G, \lift \right)$ if there is a hereditary $C^*$-subalgebra $\widetilde B \subset \widetilde A$ with a $*$-isomorphism $\lift^{\widetilde B}: B \cong \widetilde B$ such that
	\be\label{evenly_eqn}
	\forall b \in B \quad \lift\left( b\right) = \bt \text{-}\sum_{g\in G} g \lift^{\widetilde B}\left( b\right) 
	\ee
	where $\bt \text{-}\sum$ means the convergence with respect to the strict topology of $M\left( \widetilde A\right)$ (cf. the Definition \ref{strict_topology_defn} and the equation \eqref{strict_topology_eqn}).	
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}\label{cov_unital_defn}
	A  noncommutative  pre-covering $\left(A, \widetilde{A}, G, \lift \right)$ (cf. Definition \ref{fin_pre_defn}) with unital $A$ is a {\it unital noncommutative covering} if for any $\xi \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$ there is a hereditary connected $C^*$-subalgebra of $B$ {evenly covered by} $\left(A, \widetilde{A}, G, \lift \right)$ with $B \in \xi$
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}\label{cov_defn}
	Let $\left(A, \widetilde{A}, G, \lift \right)$ be a quadruple such that both $A$ and $\widetilde{A}$ are $C^*$-algebras $G \subset \Aut\left( \widetilde{A}\right)$ is a discrete subgroup and $\lift: A \hookto M\left( \widetilde{A}\right)$ is an injective $*$-homomorphism. If there is an unital noncommutative covering $\left(B, \widetilde{B}, G, \widetilde\lift \right)$  with inclusions $A \subset B$ and $\widetilde A \subset \widetilde B$ such that:
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item [(a)] both $A$ and $\widetilde A$ are essential ideals of $B$ and $\widetilde B$,
		\item[(b)] $\lift \bydef \left.\widetilde\lift\right|_A$,
		\item[(c)] the action $G \times \widetilde B \to \widetilde B$ naturally comes from the $G \times \widetilde A \to \widetilde A$.
	\end{enumerate}	
	then $\left(A, \widetilde{A}, G, \lift \right)$ is a \textit{noncommutative covering}.
\end{definition}

	


\begin{definition}\label{fund_den}
	If $A$ is a $C^*$ -algebra then a noncommutative covering $\left(A, \widetilde{A}, G, \lift \right)$ is \textit{universal}, if for any noncommutative covering $\left(A, \widetilde{A}', G', \lift' \right)$ there is natural noncommutative covering $\left(\widetilde{A}', \widetilde{A}, G'', \lift'' \right)$ with $\lift = \lift''\circ \lift'$. If the universal covering exists then $G$ is said to be the \textit{fundamental group} of $A$.
\end{definition}

\subsection{Some cohomology calculation}
\begin{lemma}\label{iso_cech_lem}
	Let  $\sX \to \sY$ is a bijective continuous map and $F$ is an Abelian group. If $\mathscr U \bydef \left\{\sU_\iota\right\}_{\iota \in I}$ is a satisfying to the hypothesis of the Theorem \ref{top_nerve_thm} covering  of $\sY$ then there are following isomorphisms
	\be
	\check H^\bullet\left(\mathscr U, F \right) \cong \check H^\bullet\left(\mathscr U, F \right)\cong \check H^\bullet\left( \sX, F \right) \cong \check H^\bullet\left(\sY, F \right) \cong  H^\bullet\left( \sX, F\right) \cong  H^\bullet\left(\sY, F \right)
	\ee
	where the notation \eqref{locally_const_not_eqn} for locally constant sheaves is used.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
	From the Lemma \ref{trivial_cech_lem} it turns out that $\mathscr U$ can be regarded as satisfying to the Theorem \ref{top_nerve_thm} covering of $\sX$. Now this lemma directly follows from the Theorem \ref{top_nerve_thm}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}\label{zero_product_lem}
	Let $F$ be an Abelian group with the natural  isomorphism $F\otimes_\Z F \cong F$.  If both $\sX$ and  $\sY$ are connected spaces with
	\bean
	H^p\left(\sX, F \right) \cong 	H^p\left(\sY, F \right) \cong  \begin{cases}
		F & p = 0\\
		\{0\} & p > 0
	\end{cases}
	\eean 
	then
	\bean
	H^p\left(\sX \times \sY, F \right) \cong \begin{cases}
		F & p = 0\\
		\{0\} & p > 0
	\end{cases}
	\eean	
	where the notation \eqref{locally_const_not_eqn} for locally constant sheaves is used.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
	If $c \in \check H^p\left(\sX \times \sY, F \right)$ then there are coverings $\mathscr U \bydef \left\{\sU_\a\right\}_{\a \in \mathscr A}$ and  $\mathscr V \bydef \left\{\sV_\bt\right\}_{\bt \in \mathscr B}$, i.e. 
	\bean
	\sX = \bigcup_{\a \in \mathscr A} \sU_\a,\\
	\sY = \bigcup_{\bt \in \mathscr B} \sV_\bt,\\
	\eean
	such that
	\bean
	c \in H^p\left( \mathscr U \times \mathscr V, F\otimes_\Z F \right)  
	\eean
	Similarly to \eqref{cup_prod_eqn} $c$ is represented by
	$$
	\sum_{j = 1} ^n\a^j_{\iota_0,...,\iota_{p_j}}\otimes  \bt^j_{\iota_{p_j},..., \iota_{p}}.
	$$
	Similarly to \eqref{cech_tau_eqn} there are maps
	\bean
	\rho: \mathscr A \onto \left\{\sX\right\},\\
	\sigma :\mathscr B \onto \left\{\sY\right\}
	\eean
	with
	\bean
	\rho^\bullet: \check C^\bullet\left( \left\{\sX\right\} F\right)\to \check C^\bullet\left( \mathscr U, F\right),\\
	\left( \rho^{p_j} \ga^j_{\iota_0,...,\iota_{p_j}}\right) \bydef \a^j_{\iota_0,...,\iota_{p_j}},\\
	\sigma^\bullet: \check C^\bullet\left( \left\{\sY\right\} F\right)\to \check C^\bullet\left( \mathscr V, F\right),\\
	\left( \sigma^{p-p_j} \dl^j_{\iota_{p_j},...,\iota_{p}}\right) \bydef \bt^j_{\iota_{p_j},...,\iota_{p}},\\
	\eean 
	where $\ga^j_{\iota_0,...,\iota_{p_j}}$ and $\dl^j_{\iota_{p_j},...,\iota_{p}}$ correspond to $\underbrace{\sX\times_\sX...\times_\sX\sX}_{p_j = \text{times}}$ and $\underbrace{\sX\times_\sX...\times_\sX\sX}_{p-p_j = \text{times}}$ respectively (cf. equation \ref{tau_c_eqn}). However from the Theorem \ref{top_nerve_thm} it follows that $c$ can be represented by 
	$$
	\sum_{j = 1} ^n\ga^j_{\iota_0,...,\iota_{p_j}}\otimes  \dl^j_{\iota_{p_j},..., \iota_{p}}.
	$$
	Also for any $j = 1, ..., n$ one can find $\mu^j \in \check C^{p_j -1}\left( \left\{\sX\right\}, F\right)$ and  $\nu^j \in \check C^{p - p_j -1}\left( \left\{\sX\right\}, F\right)$ such that
	\bean
	\ga^j_{\iota_0,...,\iota_{p_j}} = d_{p_j - 1} \mu^j,\\
	\dl^j_{\iota_{p_j},...,\iota_{p}}= = d_{p - p_j - 1} \nu^j,
	\eean 
	and taking into account \eqref{cup_product_comm_eqn} one has
	\bean
	\ga^j_{\iota_0,...,\iota_{p_j}}\otimes  \dl^j_{\iota_{p_j},..., \iota_{p}} = d_{p-1}\left( \mu^j\otimes  \dl^j_{\iota_{p_j},...,\iota_{p}}+ \left( {-1}\right) ^{p_j} \ga^j_{\iota_0,...,\iota_{p_j}}\otimes \nu^j \right). 
	\eean
	From the above equation it follows that $c = 0$.
\end{proof}


\begin{empt}\label{top_formal_fibre_empt}
	Suppose that  $\xi = \left(E, B, F, p \right)$  consists of a total space $E$, a base space $B$, 
	a fiber $F$, and a bundle projection $p: E \onto B$ such that there exists an open 
	covering $\left\{\sU\right\}$ of $B$ and, for each $\sU \in  \left\{\sU\right\}$, a  set theoretic bijection $\varphi_\sU: \sU \times F \to p^{-1}\left( \sU\right)$. Let $\xi_{\mathrm{finer}} = \left(E_{\mathrm{finer}}, B_{\mathrm{finer}}, F_{\mathrm{finer}}, p_{\mathrm{finer}} \right)$  be the fiber bundle (cf. Definition \ref{top_bundle_defn}) with bijective continuous maps
	\bean
	E_{\mathrm{finer}} \xrightarrow{\cong} E,\\
	B_{\mathrm{finer}} \xrightarrow{\cong} B,\\
	F_{\mathrm{finer}} \xrightarrow{\cong} F
	\eean  
	and commutative  diagram
	\bean
	\begin{tikzcd}
		E_{\mathrm{finer}} \arrow[d, "p_{\mathrm{finer}}"] \arrow[r, "\cong"] & E \arrow[d, "p"]\\
		B_{\mathrm{finer}} \arrow[r, "\cong"]	& B
	\end{tikzcd}
	\eean
	Assume for each $\sU \in  \left\{\sU\right\}$, a  set theoretic bijection $\varphi_\sU: \sU \times F \to p^{-1}\left( \sU\right)$ naturally yields a homeomorphism  
	$$
	\varphi_{\sU_{\mathrm{finer}}}: \sU_{\mathrm{finer}} \times F_{\mathrm{finer}} \to p^{-1}\left( \sU_{\mathrm{finer}}\right)
	$$
	Let $M$ is and Abelian group with isomorphism $M \cong M\otimes_\sZ M$. Let $\left\{\sU\right\}$ (resp. $\left\{\sV\right\}$) be and open covering of $B$ (resp $F$) having the property that $H^p\left( \sU_{\sigma};M\right)= 0$  (resp  $H^p\left( \sV_{\rho};M \right)= 0$  for $p > 0$ and
	all $\sigma \in K\left(\sU\right)$ (resp. all $\rho\in K\left(\sV\right)$) in the nerves of coverings (cf. Definition \ref{nerve_defn})
\end{empt}
\begin{definition}\label{top_formal_fibre_defn}
	Under the hypothesis \ref{top_formal_fibre_empt}  $\xi = \left(E, B, F, p \right)$ is a {\it formal fiber bundle}
\end{definition}
\begin{theorem}\label{top_formal_fibre_thm}
	$\xi = \left(E, B, F, p \right)$ is a { formal fiber bundle} then for any $p > 0$ one has the natural isomorphism 
	\be
	H^*\left(E, M  \right) \cong  H^*\left(E_{\mathrm{finer}}, M \right)
	\ee
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
	According to the Lemma  \ref{zero_product_lem} one should prove that the homomorphism \eqref{h_ctr_eqn} is an isomorphism.
	One has
	\be\label{projective_union_eqn}
	E = \bigcup_{\substack{\sU \in \{\sU\} \\ \sV \in \{\sV\} }} \sU \times \sV
	\ee
	Both $\{\sU\}$ and $\{\sV\}$ satisfy  to the Theorem \ref{top_nerve_thm}, so one has 
	$$
	\forall p > 0\quad \forall \sU\in K\left( \{\sU\}\right) \quad  \forall \sV \in  K\left(\{\sV\}\right)\quad H^p\left(\sU \right) = H^p\left(\sV \right)= \{0\}
	$$
	and taking into account the Lemma  \eqref{zero_product_lem} one has
	\bean
	\forall p > 0\quad \forall \sU\in K\left( \{\sU\}\right) \quad  \forall \sV \in  K\left(\{\sV\}\right)\quad H^p\left(\sU\times \sV \right)= \{0\}
	\eean 
	Any product $\sU \times \mathcal W\subset E$ is open in both $E$ and $(E_{\mathrm{finer}}$. This lemma follows from the Theorem \ref{top_nerve_thm} the proof is similar to the \ref{compact_thm} one.
	
\end{proof}

	
	\subsection{Hausdorff blowing-up}
	\subsubsection{Basic construction}	
	\begin{definition}\label{blowing_defn}
		If $A$ is a $C^*$-algebra then an inclusion $\mathfrak {Blowing}_{\sX-A }:C_0\left( \sX\right) \hookto M\left(A \right)$  (or equivalently $C_0\left( \sX\right) \subset M\left(A \right)$ ) is \textit{Hausdorff blowing-up} of $A$ if  both sets
		\be\label{blowing_eqn}
		\begin{split}
			C_c\left( \sX\right)A \bydef \left\{fa| f \in C_c\left( \sX\right)\quad a \in A \right\},\\
			AC_c\left( \sX\right) \bydef \left\{af| f \in C_c\left( \sX\right)\quad a \in A \right\}
		\end{split}
		\ee
		are dense in $A$.
	\end{definition}
	
	\begin{remark}\label{blowing_rem}
		$C_c\left( \sX\right)A$ is dense in $A$ if and only if $AC_c\left( \sX\right)$ is dense in $A$ (cf. equations \eqref{blowing_eqn}), i.e. both equations iuclusions  \eqref{blowing_eqn} are equivalent.
	\end{remark}
\begin{remark}
	The inclusion $
\mathfrak{Blowing}_{\sX-A }:C_0\left( \sX\right) \hookto M\left(A \right)$ can be uniquely extended up to
\be\label{blowing_p_eqn}
\mathfrak{Blowing}^+_{\sX-A }:C\left( \sX^+\right) \hookto M\left(A \right)
\ee
such that $\sX^+$ is the one-point compactification  of $\sX$ (cf. Definition \ref{top_compactification_defn}) and $\mathfrak{Blowing}^+_{\sX-A }\left( 1_{C\left( \sX^+\right)}\right) \bydef 1_{M\left(A \right) }$
\end{remark}

	
	
	%\begin{empt}\label{blowing_k_theory_empt}
	%	If $A$ be is  stable $C^*$-algebra then $A \cong \K\otimes A\cong A\otimes \K$. Moreover  if  $C_0\left( \sY\right) \subset M\left( A\right)$ be Hausdorff blowing-up then one has a  natural action 
	%	\bean
	%	C_0\left(\sY \right)\times  \left(A\otimes \K \right)\to A\otimes \K
	%	% \left(\K\otimes A\right)\times C_0\left(\sY \right)\to A\otimes \K 
	%	\eean 
	%	Using it one can one can construct an  injective $*$-homomorphism  	%	$$
	%	\left(C_0\left(\sY \right) \otimes \K \right) \to A
	%	$$
	%	This homomorphism yields homomorphisms of $K$-theory
	%	\bea\label{blowing_k0_eqn}
	%	K^0\left(\sY \right)\cong K_0\left(C_0\left( \sY\right)  \right) \to K_0\left( A\right),\\\label{blowing_k1_eqn}
	%	K^1\left(\sY \right)\cong K_1\left(C_0\left( \sY\right)  \right) \to K_1\left( A\right).
	%	\eea 
	%	If $A$ is an  irrational rotation algebra of torus then the map $K_1\left(C_0\left( \sY\right)  \right) \to K_1\left( A\right)$ is an isomorphism.
	%\end{empt}
	%\begin{example}\label{blowing_hausdorff_exm}	If $A$ is a  given by \eqref{cross_mult_eqn} $C^*$-algebra with Hausdorff spectrum $\sX$  then from the Theorems \ref{oa_haus_prim_thm} and  \ref{dauns_hofmann_thm} one has the natural inclusion $C_0\left(\sX \right) \hookto M\left( A\right)$, which is Hausdorff blowing-up.
	%\end{example}
	
	\begin{exercise}\label{haus_foli_exer}
		Prove that the  given by the equation \eqref{groupoid_multiplier_eqn} *-homomorphism
		\be\label{h_groupoid_multiplier_eqn}
	C_0\left(\G^0 \right) \hookto M\left(  C^*_r\left(\G, \sigma \right)\right).
	\ee
	is Hausdorff blowing-up.
	\end{exercise}

	
	\begin{definition}\label{blowing_ideals_au_ua_defn}
		Let  $ C_0\left( \sX\right)\subset  M\left( A\right) $ be  Hausdorff blowing-up of $A$ (cf. Definition \ref{blowing_defn}), and let $\sU \subset \sX$ be an open subset. Both   left and right  closed ideals $A_\sU$  and $_\sU A$ of $A$ generated by sets 	$AC_0\left( \sU\right)$ and $C_0\left( \sU\right)A$ are the \textit{left} $\sU$-\textit{ideal} and the \textit{right} $\sU$-\textit{ideal} respectively. A hereditary $C^*$-subalgebra of $A$
		\be\label{blowing_hereditary_u_eqn} 
		\begin{split}
			_\sU A_\sU \bydef	~	_\sU A\cap  A_\sU = A^*	_\sU \cap  A_\sU\\ %(\text{cf. Definition \ref{hered_defn} and the Lemma \ref{hered_bab_lem}}).
		\end{split}
		\ee	
		is the $ \sU$-\textit{subalgebra}.
		
	\end{definition}
	
	
	\begin{lemma}\label{blowing_compact_lem}
		If $C\cong C_0\left( \sY\right) \subset M\left(A \right)$ is    {Hausdorff blowing-up} of $A$  (cf. Definition \ref{blowing_defn}	for any $a \in A$ and $\eps > 0$ following conditions hold:
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item[(i)] there is a positive $f \in C_c\left( \sY\right)_+$ with 
			\be\label{blowing_compact_eqn}
			\begin{split}
				\left\| f  \right\| \le 1,\\
				\left\| a - af  \right\|< \eps,\\
				\left\| a - fa \right\|< \eps,\\
				\left\| a - faf  \right\|< \eps,
			\end{split}
			\ee
			\item[(ii)] there are an open subset $\sU \subset \sY$ with compact closure and $b \in ~_\sU A_\sU$ such that
			\be\label{blowing_compact_b_eqn}
			\begin{split}
				b \in  ~_\sU A_\sU,\\
				\left\| a - b \right\|< \eps.
			\end{split}
			\ee
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{lemma}
	\begin{proof}(i)
		If $g \in C_c\left( \sY\right)$ then $g = fg = gf$ for any positive $f \in C_c\left( \sY\right)_+$ such that
		\bean
		\left\| f \right\|= 1,\\
		f\left(\supp g \right) = 1.
		\eean 
		If $f' \in C_c\left( \sY\right)$ and $c' \in A$ such that
		$\left\|a-f'c' \right\| < \eps/4$ (cf. equation \eqref{blowing_eqn}) then there for any positive $f_1$ such that $\left\| f_1 \right\|= 1$, $~f_1\left(\supp f' \right) = 1$ one has
		\bean
		\left\|f_1\left( a-f'c \right) \right\|\le \left\|f_1 \right\|\left\|a-f'c \right\|\le \frac{\eps}{4},\\
		\left\|a-f_1a \right\| < \left\|f_1a - f_1f'c\right\|+ \left\|a - f_1f'c\right\|\le \frac{\eps}{2}
		\eean
		Similarly 	If $f'' \in C_c\left( \sY\right)$ and $c''/ \in A$ such that
		$\left\|a-f'c'' \right\| < \eps/4$ then for any positive for any positive $f_2$ such that $\left\| f_2 \right\|= 1$, $~f_1\left(\supp f' \right) = 1$ one has
		\bean
		\left\|a-a f_2 \right\| <  \frac{\eps}{2}
		\eean
		If $f = \max\left(f_1, f_2 \right)$ then $f\left(\supp f' \cup \supp f'' \right)= \{1\}$ 
		and
		\bean
		\begin{split}
			\left\| f  \right\| \le 1,\\
			\left\| a - af  \right\|< \frac{\eps}{2},\\
			\left\| a - fa \right\|< \frac{\eps}{2},\\
		\end{split}
		\eean
		On the other hand
		\bean
		\left\| a - faf \right\|\le \left\| a - fa \right\|+ \left\| fa - faf \right\|< \frac{\eps}{2}+ 	\left\| f\right\|\left\|a - fa\right\|< \eps.
		\eean
		(ii) The set $\sU \bydef \left\{y \in \sY | f\left(y\right)\neq 0\right\}\subset \sY$ is open and closure of $\sU$ is the compact set $\supp f$. Moreover  $f a f \in ~_\sU A_\sU$ and  $\left\|a - faf\right\|< \eps$.
		
	\end{proof}
	%\begin{empt}\label{blowing_compact_supp_empt}
	%	If $\left\{\sU_\la\right\}_{\la\in\La}$ is a given by the Corollary	\ref{top_connected_union_cor} family of open subsets of $\sY$ with compact closures then $\sY = \cup_{\la \in \La} \sU_\la$. Since the family is directed the union $A_c \bydef \cup_{\la \in \La} \sU_\la$ is a $*$-subalgebra of $A$. From the Lemma \ref{blowing_compact_lem} it follows that $A_c$ is dense in $A$.
	%\end{empt}
	%\begin{definition}\label{blowing_compact_supp_defn}
	%	The given by \ref{blowing_compact_supp_empt} dense $*$-subalgebra $A_c \subset A$ is said to be the \textit{algebra of compactly supported elements}.
	%\end{definition}
	
	
	\begin{empt} 
		
		We leave to the reader a proof of following equations:
		\be\label{blowing_su_eqn}
		\begin{split}
			_\sU A \bydef \left\{ a \in A~ |~ \forall f \in C_0\left( \sY\right)\quad f\left(\sU \right)= \{0\}  \quad \Rightarrow \quad fa = 0\right\} ,\\
			A_\sU \bydef \left\{ a \in A~ |~ \forall f \in C_0\left( \sY\right)\quad  f\left(\sU \right)= \{0\} \quad \Rightarrow \quad af = 0\right\}
		\end{split}
		\ee
		
		
		\bea\label{blowing_sue1_eqn}
		\sU'\cap \sU'' =\emptyset\quad \Rightarrow\quad A_{\sU'}~_{\sU''}A= \{0\}.
		\eea
		
		From \eqref{blowing_su_eqn} it follows that
		\be\label{blowing_su_inc_eqn}
		\sU'\subset \sU'' \quad \Rightarrow\quad _{\sU'}A \subset~  _{\sU''}A ~\text{ AND } ~A_{\sU'}\subset A_{\sU''}~\text{ AND }~  _{\sU'}A _{\sU'}\subset _{\sU''}A _{\sU''}.
		\ee
	\end{empt}
	
	\begin{definition}\label{blowing_support_defn}
		If $C_0\left( \sX\right) \subset M\left(A \right)$ is    {Hausdorff blowing-up} of $A$  (cf. Definition \ref{blowing_defn}),  $a \in A$ and
		$
		\sU_a \bydef\bigcap 
		\left\{\left.{\sU} \subset \sX\right| a\in~_\sU A_{\sU} \right\}
		$
		then the  closure $\sV_a$  of $\sU_a$ is said to be the \textit{support} of $a$. We write $\supp a \bydef \sV_a$.
	\end{definition}
	
	\begin{lemma}\label{pedersen_eps_lem}
		Let $\eps > 0$, and let 	 $f_\eps: \R \to \R$ be a continuous function given by 
		\begin{equation}\label{f_eps_eqn}
			f_\eps\left( x\right)  \bydef\left\{
			\begin{array}{c l}
				0 &x \le \eps \\
				x - \eps & x > \eps
			\end{array}\right.
		\end{equation}
		If $A$ is a $C^*$-algebra 
		then one has
		\bea\label{k0_ped_e_eqn}
		K\left( A \right)_0 = \left\{f_\eps \left(a\right) \left|~a \in A_+, \quad \eps > 0 \right.\right\},~~~\\
		\label{kp_ped_e_eqn}
		K\left( A \right)_+ = \left\{a \in A_+ \left|a \le \sum_{j = 1}^n f_{\eps_j}\left(  a_j\right) \quad a_j \in  	K\left( A \right)_0\quad \eps_j > 0\quad j=1,...,n\right.\right\}~~
		\eea
		where both $	K\left( A \right)_0$ and 	$K\left( A \right)_+$ are given by equations \eqref{pedersen_k0_eqn} and \eqref{pedersen_k_plus_eqn} respectively
	\end{lemma}
	\begin{proof}
		If  $a\in A_+$ and $\eps > 0$ then $f_\eps \left(a\right)= \phi_\eps\left(a \right)$ where  $\phi_\eps \in K(]0, \infty [$ is given by 
		\bean
		\phi_\eps\left( x\right)  =\left\{
		\begin{array}{c l}
			0 &x \le \eps \\
			x - \eps &  \eps \le x \le \left\| a\right\|\\
			2	\left\| a\right\| - \eps - x & \left\| a\right\| \le x \le 2\left\| a\right\|-\eps\\
			0 & x \ge 2 \left\| a\right\| -\eps\\
		\end{array}\right.
		\eean
		It follows that $f_\eps\left(a\right)	\in K\left( A \right)_0$. Conversely  if $a \in	K\left( A \right)_0$ then from \eqref{pedersen_k0_eqn} it turns out that there is $b \in A_+$ and $\varphi \in   K(]0, \infty [$ such that $a = \varphi\left(b\right)$. If  $\supp \varphi \subset \left[\eps, c\right]$ and  $\psi \in C_c\left( \R\right)_+$ is given by
		\bean
		\psi\left( x\right)  =\left\{
		\begin{array}{c l}
			0 &x \le 0 \\
			x &0 \le x \le \eps \\
			\varphi\left(x\right) + \eps &\eps \le x \le c \\
			\eps + c - x&  c \le x \le c+ \eps\\
			0 & x \ge c + \eps
		\end{array}\right.
		\eean
		then $ \varphi = f_\eps  \circ\psi$. It follows that $a = f_\eps\left(b' \right)$ where $b' \bydef \psi\left(b\right)$. So the equation \eqref{k0_ped_e_eqn} is proven. The equation \eqref{kp_ped_e_eqn} is a direct consequence of \eqref{k0_ped_e_eqn} and \eqref{pedersen_k_plus_eqn} ones.
		
	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	
	
	\begin{lemma}\label{blowing_pedersen_compact_lem}
		If  $C_0\left( \sX\right)\hookto M\left( A\right)$ is Hausdorff blowing-up and $a\in A$ belongs to the Pedersen's ideal $K\left(A \right)$ (cf. Definition \ref{pedersen_ideal_defn}) then the support of $a$ (cf. Definition \ref{blowing_support_defn}) is compact.
	\end{lemma}
	\begin{proof}
		If $a \in K\left(A\right)_0$ (cf \eqref{pedersen_k0_eqn}) then from the Lemma  \eqref{pedersen_eps_lem} it follows that there is $\eps > 0$ and $b \in A_+$ such that $a = f_\eps \left( b\right)$ where $f_\eps$ is given by \eqref{f_eps_eqn}. On the other hand  there is a positive element   $c\in  A_+$  such that $\left\|c - b \right\|  < \eps/2$ and $\supp c$ is compact (cf. Definition  \ref{blowing_defn}).
		If $a \le c$ does not hold and $\rho: A \hookto B\left(\H \right)$ is a faithful  nondegenerate representation  then there is $\xi \in \H$ such that
		\bean\label{blowing_ac_eqn}
		\forall \xi \in \H \quad \left( \xi, \rho\left( a \right) \xi\right) > \left( \xi, \rho\left( c \right) \xi\right)
		\eean
		From $\left\|c - b \right\|  < \eps/2$ if follows that
		\be\label{blowing_acc_eqn}
		\forall \xi \in \H  \quad \left\| \xi \right\| = 1\quad \Rightarrow\quad  \left|\left( \xi, \rho\left( b \right) \xi\right)-\left( \xi, \rho\left( c \right) \xi\right) \right| < \eps/2
		\ee
		On the other hand from $a =f_\eps \left( b\right)> 0$ it follows that there is $\xi \in \H$ and $\la \in \R_+$ such that
		\bean
		\left\| \xi \right\| = 1,\\
		\rho\left(a \right) \xi = \la \xi,\\
		\rho\left(b \right)\xi = \left( \la+\eps \right) \xi,\\
		\rho\left(a \right)\xi = \la  \xi,\\
		\left( \xi, \rho\left( b \right) \xi\right) - \left( \xi, \rho\left( a \right) \xi\right)= \eps
		\eean
		and taking into account \eqref{blowing_acc_eqn} one has
		$$
		\left( \xi, \rho\left( c \right) \xi\right)- \left( \xi, \rho\left( a \right) \xi\right)> \frac{\eps}{2}
		$$
		Above condition contradicts with \eqref{blowing_ac_eqn} so $a \le c$.
		If $\supp a \subsetneqq \supp c$ then there is a nonempty  open set  $\sU \subset \supp a\setminus \supp c$. For any $f \in C_0\left(\sU \right)\setminus \{0\}$ one has
		\bean
		faf^* > 0,\\
		fcf^* = 0.
		\eean
		However it is impossible since $a \le c$, so $\supp a \subsetneqq \supp c$ is not true and $\supp a \subset\supp c$. Thus the set $\supp a$ is a closed subset of the compact set $\supp c$ therefore $\supp a$ is compact. Using this fact and the Definition \ref{pedersen_ideal_defn} we conclude that $\supp a$ is compact for any $a \in K\left( A\right)$. 
	\end{proof}
	\begin{remark}
		The Lemma \ref{blowing_pedersen_compact_lem} can be regarded as a generalization of the equation  \eqref{peder_c0_eqn}.
	\end{remark}
	
	\begin{remark}\label{blow_rem}
		From the equation  \eqref{peder_c0_eqn} it follows that the injective homomorphism $\varphi_\sX : C_0\left(\sX \right) \hookto M\left(A \right)$ is good (cf. Definition \ref{good_defn}). So there is the natural surjective continuous map
		\be\label{phi_a_eqn}
		\phi_A : \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right) \onto \sX.
		\ee
	\end{remark}
	\begin{empt}
		
		If $C_0\left(\sY \right) \xrightarrow{f} M\left(A \right)$ is Hausdorff blowing-up then 
		from the Remark \ref{blow_rem} and the Proposition \ref{spectral_sequence_prop} it follows that
		\begin{enumerate}	
			\item [(i)] 
			if $\mathscr A$ is sheaf of  Abelian groups in $\sY$ then we have a homomorphism $H^q\left(\sY, \mathscr A \right) \xrightarrow{} H^q \left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right) , \phi_A^*\mathscr A\right)$ for each $q$ which is functorial in $f$ and natural in $\mathscr A$.
			\item [(ii)] If $\mathscr B$ is a sheaf of Abelian groups in $\sX$ then we have a spectral sequence (Leray spectral sequence) $H^p\left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right) , R^q\left(\phi_A \right) _*\left(\mathscr B \right) \right)\Rightarrow H^{p + q}\left(\sX, \mathscr B \right)$ which is natural in $ \mathscr B$.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{empt}
	!!!
	\begin{empt}\label{blowing_empt}
		Let $A$ be a $C^*$-algebra with the spectrum $\sY$ such that
		\be\label{norm_eqn}
		\forall a \in A\quad \left\|a \right\| = \sup_{y \in \sY} \left\| \rho_y\left(a \right) \right\| 
		\ee
		where $\rho_y: A \to B\left(\H_y \right)$ is the corresponding to $y$ irreducible representation. 
	\end{empt}
	\begin{empt}
		
		If $C^*$-algebra $A$ satisfies to \eqref{norm_eqn}, $\sY$ is the spectrum of $A$ and $S\subsetneqq A$ is a closed subset then there is $a \in A\setminus S$ and $\eps > 0$ such that
		$$
		\forall a' \in S\quad  \left\| a - a' \right\| > 2\eps
		$$
		It turns out that there is $y \in \sY$ such that
		$$
		\forall a' \in S\quad  \left\| \rho_y\left(a - a' \right) \right\| > \eps
		$$
		If $L\subset A$ is a proper closed left ideal then there is $y \in \sY$ such that
		\be\label{to_sp_eqn}
		\rho_y\left( L\right) \H_y \neq \H_y.
		\ee
		If for all  $\xi \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$  such that there is a bicommutant (cf, Definition \ref{bicommutant_defn}) $\xi'' \subset A$ then there is the unique $y \in \sY$ such that $\rho_y\left( L\right) \H_y \neq \H_y$. It turns out that there are following maps
		\be\label{gg_m_eqn}
		\begin{split}
			\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right) \to \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)'' \to \sY.
		\end{split}
		\ee
		The maps \ref{gg_m_eqn} are specializations of \eqref{to_sp_eqn} ones.
		If there is a map $\sX \xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Blowing}} \sY$ such that the following diagram commutative 
		\newline
		\begin{tikzcd}
			\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right)	 \arrow[rr, "\phi_A"]\arrow[rd]  & ~ & \sX \arrow[ld, , "\mathfrak{Blowing}"]\\
			& \sY &
		\end{tikzcd}
		\\
		then $\mathfrak{Blowing}$ is said to be \textit{blowing - up}.
	\end{empt}
		\begin{remark}
		then we say that $\mathfrak{Blowing}$ is the Hausdorff blowing-up of the spectrum.
		The "blowing-up" word is inspired by following reasons:
		\begin{itemize}
			\item the existence  of the  surjective  map $\mathfrak{Blowing}$ from the  Hausdorff space  to the spectrum, %(cf. Definition \ref{blowing_spectral_defn}),
			\item  in the algebraic geometry   "blowing-up" means  from a map $\sX \to \sY$ such that the variety $\sX$ has no singular points (cf. \cite{hartshorne:ag}).
		\end{itemize}
	\end{remark}
	
	\subsubsection{Natural blowing-up}	

\paragraph*{}
	If $A$ is a $C^*$-algebra and  $C_0\left( \sX\right) \to M\left(A \right)$ is Hausdorff blowing-up then the action $C_b\left(
	\sX \right) \times C_c\left(\sX \right)\to  C_c\left(\sX \right)$ yields  the action $C_b\left(
	\sX \right) \times\left(  C_c\left(\sX \right) A\right) \to  C_c\left(\sX \right)A$. Since $  C_c\left(\sX \right)A$ is dense in $A$ one the action $C_b\left(
	\sX \right) \times\left(  C_c\left(\sX \right) A\right) \to  C_c\left(\sX \right)A$ can be naturally extended up to the action $C_b\left(
	\sX \right) \times A \to  A$. Similarly one has the natural right action $A \times C_b\left(
	\sX \right) \to  A$. One can prove that both these actions yield an inclusion
	\be\label{blowing_b_eqn} 
	C_b\left(\sX \right)\to M\left(A \right).  
\ee


\begin{definition}\label{blowing_uni_defn}
	Let $A$ be a $C^*$-algebra. Consider a category $\mathfrak{Hausdorff}\left(A\right)$ such that 
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item[(a)] any object of $\mathfrak{Hausdorff}\left(A\right)$ is Hausdorff blowing-up, 
		\item[(b)] a morphism from $C_0\left( \sX'\right) \hookto M\left(A \right)$ to $C_0\left( \sX''\right) \hookto M\left(A \right)$ is an injective *-homeomorphism $C_b\left( \sX'\right) \hookto C_b\left( \sX''\right)$ such that the diagram 
		such that the diagram 
		\newline
		\begin{tikzcd}
			&M\left(A \right)   & \\
			C_b\left(\sX' \right)  \arrow[rr]\arrow[ru]	&& 	C_b\left(\sX'' \right)
			\arrow[lu]
		\end{tikzcd}
		\\
		is commutative (cf the equation \eqref{blowing_b_eqn}).
	\end{enumerate}
		The final object (cf. Definition \ref{terminal_ob_defn})of this category $C_0\left( \sX\right) \hookto M\left(A \right)$ is  \textit{universal Hausdorff blowing-up of $A$}.  Hausdorff blowing-up $C\left(\sX \right)   \to M\left( A\right)$ is {\it maximal}  if for any Hausdorff blowing-up $C_0\left(\sX' \right)   \to M\left( A\right)$ with the commutative diagram
			\newline
		\begin{tikzcd}
			&M\left(A \right)   & \\
			C_0\left(\sX' \right)  \arrow[rr, "
			\cong "]\arrow[ru]	&& 	C_b\left(\sX \right)
			\arrow[lu]
		\end{tikzcd}
		\\
		the $*$-homomorphism $C_0\left(\sX' \right)\hookto C_0\left(\sX\right)$ is an isomorphism.
		
\end{definition}	
\begin{remark}
From the Theorem \ref{zorn_thm} it follows that a maximal Hausdorff blowing-up always exists.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}\label{hausdorff_defn}
	Let $\sX$ be a topological space. The $\sX$-{\it Hausdorff category} (cf. Definition \ref{category_defn}) $\mathfrak{Hausdorff}\left( \sX\right)$ is such that 
	
	\begin{itemize}
		\item objects of $\mathfrak{Hausdorff}\left( \sX\right)$ are continuous surjective maps $\sX \onto \sY$ onto Hausdorff locally compact space, 
		\item a morphism form $\sX \onto \sY'$ to $\sX \onto \sY''$ is a continuous surjective map  $\sY' \onto \sY''$ such that the diagram 
		\newline
		\begin{tikzcd}
			&\sX \arrow[ld] \arrow[rd] & \\
			\sY' \arrow[rr]	&& \sY''
		\end{tikzcd}
		\\
		is commutative.
	\end{itemize}
	
\end{definition}

	\begin{lemma}
	For any topological space $\sX$ there is the initial object (cf. Definition \ref{initial_ob_defn}) of the  $\sX$-{Hausdorff category}.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
	Let $A$ be a commutative $C^*$-algebra of all bonded continuous maps from $\sX$ to $\C$ and let $\sY'$ be the spectrum of $A$ (cf. Definition \ref{spectrum_prime_primtive_defn}).  Any $x \in \sX$ yields the maximal ideal 
	$$
	I_x \bydef \left\{ f \in A | f\left( x\right) = 0\right\}
	$$
	From the Theorem \ref{gelfand-naimark_thm} the ideal $I_x$ yield a point $y \in \sY'$. So there is the natural  map $\phi' :\sX \to \sY'$. If $\sY \bydef \phi"\left( \sX\right)$ then $\phi'$ yields  the surjective map  $\phi :\sX \onto \sY$. One can prove that the map is continuous. From the Theorem \ref{gelfand-naimark_thm} it turns out that the spaces $\sY'$ and $\sY$ are locally compact and Hausdorff. One can prove that the map $\phi$ is continuous. If there is and an object $\sX \onto \sY''$ with nonidentical morphism $\phi'' : \sY''\onto \sY$ then there are $y_1, y_2 \in \sY''$ with $y_1 \neq y_2$ and $\phi''\left( y_1\right) = \phi''\left( y_2\right)$. There is $f \in C_0\left( \sY''\right)$ such that $f\left( y_1\right)  \neq f\left( y_2\right)$. Clearly $f \in A$ but $f \notin C_0\left(
	\sY \right)$ i.e. $C_0\left(\sY \right)  \subsetneqq A$. It is a contradiction which proves that the existence jf $\sY''$ is impossible.  
	
\end{proof}
\begin{definition}\label{blowing_uni_h_defn}
	The initial object of the category $\sX$-{Hausdorff category} is the	$\sX$ - \textit{universal Hausdorff quotient space}.
\end{definition}


\begin{definition}\label{top_characteristic_function_defn}
	If $\sX$ is a set and $\sU \subset \sX$ is a compact set  then the map 
	\be\label{top_char_f_eqn}
	\begin{split}
		\chi_\sU : \sX \to \R,\\
		x \mapsto	\begin{cases}
			1 & x \in \sU\\
			0 & x \in \sX\setminus \sU
		\end{cases}
	\end{split}
	\ee
	is the \textit{characteristic function} of $\sU$.
\end{definition}
\begin{rem}
If $\sX$ is a Hausdorff, locally compact space and $D\left( \sX\right)$ is a $C^*$-algebra of bounded maps from $\sX$ to $\C$ then one can proof that  for any $f \in C_0\left( \sX\right)$  there is a $C^*$-norm limit
\be
f = \lim_{\la\in \La} \sum_{j = 1}^n c_{\la,j} \chi_{\sU_{\la,j}}
\ee
where $c_{\la,j}\in \C$ and  $\chi_{\sU_{\la,j}}$ is a characteristic function \ref{top_characteristic_function_defn}.
\end{rem}
\begin{empt}\label{blowing_natural_empt}
Let $A$ be a $C^*$-algebra, and let $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right)$ be the Gelfand space $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right)$ (cf. Definition \ref{gelfand_space_defn}) of $A$. Let $\sY$ be  the $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right)$ - {universal Hausdorff quotient space} (cf. Definition \ref{blowing_uni_h_defn}). For any open subset $\sU \subset \sY$ there is an open subset of $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right)$ so one has a closed ideal $L_\sU$ (cf. Definition \ref{gelfand_space_defn}). If $A \hookto B\left(\sH \right)$ is a faithful nondegenerate representation (cf. Definitions \ref{faithful_repr_defn} and \ref{nondegenerate_repr_defn}) then $L_\sU\H$ is a closed subspace of $\H$. For any $f\in C_0\left( \sY\right)$  there is $a_f \in B\left( \H\right)$ such that
\bean
f = \lim_{\la\in \La} \sum_{j = 1}^n c_{\la,j} \chi_{\sU_{\la,j}}\quad \Leftrightarrow \quad a_f = \lim_{\la\in \La} \sum_{j = 1}^n c_{\la,j} p_{\sU_{\la,j}}
\eean 
 where $p_{\sU_{\la,j}}$ is the projector onto the subspace $L_{\sU_{\la,j}}\H \subset \H$. We leave to the reader the proof of the $C^*$-norm convergence of the above limit. The map $f \mapsto a_f$ is a representation
 \be\label{blowing_natural_eqn}
 \pi_{\sY } : C_0\left(\sY \right) \hookto B\left(
 \H \right) 
 \ee
\end{empt}
\begin{definition}\label{blowing_natural_defn}
Under the hypothesis \ref{blowing_natural_empt} if any $a \in  \pi_{\sY } \left(  C_0\left(\sY \right)\right)$ is the multiplier of $A$ (cf. Definition \ref{multiplier_el_defn}) and the corresponding inclusion $C_0\left( \sY\right) \subset  M\left(A \right)$ is Hausdorff blowing-up then we say that $C_0\left( \sY\right) \subset  M\left(A \right)$ is {\it natural Hausdorff blowing-up}.
\end{definition}
\begin{remark}
Any natural Hausdorff blowing-up is universal (cf. Definition \ref{blowing_uni_defn}).
\end{remark}
	\subsubsection{Homomorphisms of $K$-theory}
\paragraph*{}	
If $A$ is a $C^*$-algebra and  $C_0\left( \sX\right)\subset M\left(A\otimes \K \right)$ is natural Hausdorff blowing-up (cf. Definition \ref{blowing_natural_defn}) then there is a given by \eqref{blowing_p_eqn} homomorphism 	$\mathfrak{Blowing}^+_{\sX-A\otimes \K }:C\left( \sX^+\right) \hookto M\left(A\otimes \K \right)$ and there is a diagram

\be\label{chern_eqn}
\begin{tikzcd}
	\mathbb{M}_\infty \left( A^+\right)  \ar[r,hook, "\phi"] & A^+ \otimes \ar[rd,hook, "\phi_A"]  \K &\\
	& & 	 M\left(A\otimes \K\right)\cong  M\left(A\otimes \K\otimes \K\right)  \\
	& \mathbb{M}_\infty \left(C\left( \sX^+\right) \right) \ar[ru,hook, "\phi_\sX"]&
\end{tikzcd}
\ee
\begin{definition}\label{chern_defn}
	Let  $\sV\in V\left(A^+ \right)$ be an equivalence class of projections represented by $e_A\in 	\mathbb{M}_\infty \left( A^+\right)$ (cf. Definition \ref{projection_equivalence_defn}) such that there is the unique class  $\sV_\sX\in V\left(C\left(\sX^+ \right) \right) $ represented by $e_\sX\in 	\mathbb{M}_\infty \left(C\left( \sX^+\right) \right)$ with $\phi_A \circ \phi\left(e_A \right)\sim\phi_\sX\left( e_\sX\right)$ where $\sim$ is given by the Definition \ref{projection_equivalence_defn}. 
	The  {\it Chern classes} $c_j\left(\sV \right)\in H^{2j}\left(\sX^+, \Z \right)$ of $\sV$ are {Chern classes} $c_j\left(\sV_\sX \right)$ of $\sV_\sX$ (cf. Theorem \ref{chern_class_thm}), i.e.
	\be\label{chern_defn_eqn}
\forall j\in \N \quad c_j\left(\sV \right)\bydef c_j\left(\sV_\sX \right)
	\ee 
\end{definition}
\paragraph{title}
If $A$ is a $C^*$-algebra and  $C_0\left( \sX\right)\subset M\left(A \right)$ is natural Hausdorff blowing-up (cf. Definition \ref{blowing_natural_defn}) then there is a given by \eqref{blowing_p_eqn} homomorphism 	$\mathfrak{Blowing}^+_{\sX-A }:C\left( \sX^+\right) \hookto M\left(A \right)$ and there are pullback
diagrams
\bean
\begin{tikzcd}
~
	& A  \arrow[d, "\varphi^2"] & & \mathrm{Proj}^{\mathrm{nat}}\left(A \right) \arrow[r, "\subset"] \arrow[d, "\varphi_*"]& \mathrm{Proj}\left( A\right)   \arrow[d, "\varphi^2_*"]\\
	C\left( \sX^+\right) \arrow[r, "\varphi^1"]	& M\left( A\right)& & 	\mathrm{Proj}\left( C\left( \sX^+\right)\right)  \arrow[r, "\varphi^1_*"]	& \mathrm{Proj}\left( M\left( A\right)\right) 
\end{tikzcd}
\eean
(cf. Definition \ref{proj_v_defn}) where  $\sX^+$ is the one point  compactification  of $\sX$ (cf. Definition \ref{top_compactification_defn}).

\begin{empt}
Under the above hypothesis there are left and right actions
\bean
C\left( \sX^+\right)  \times \left( A \otimes 
\K\right) \to A \otimes \K,\\
\left(f , a \otimes x \right) \mapsto fa \otimes x;\\
\left( A\otimes \K \right) \times  C\left( \sX^+\right)  \to A \otimes \K,\\
\left(a \otimes x, f  \right) \mapsto af \otimes x.
\eean
So there is an inclusion
$
C\left( \sX^+\right) \subset M\left(A\otimes \K \right)$ and  diagrams
\bean
\begin{tikzcd}
A \arrow[r, "-\otimes p_1"] 	& A \otimes \K \arrow[d, "\varphi^2"]\\
	C\left( \sX^+\right) \arrow[r, "\varphi^1"]	& M\left( A\right) \otimes \K \\
	 \mathrm{Proj}^{\mathrm{nat}}\left(A \right) \arrow[r, "\subset"] %\arrow[d, "\varphi_*"]
	 &\mathrm{Proj}\left(A \right) \arrow[r, "\otimes p_1"]& \mathrm{Proj}\left( A\otimes \K\right)   \arrow[d, "\varphi_*\otimes p_1"]\\
	 	\mathrm{Proj}\left( C\left( \sX^+\right)\right) \arrow[rr, "\mathfrak{Blowing}\otimes p_1"] &	& \mathrm{Proj}\left( M\left( A\right) \otimes \K\right)
\end{tikzcd}
\eean
where $p_1$ is a rank-one projector in $\K$
\bean
 \mathrm{Proj}^{\mathrm{nat}}\left(A \right)\bydef \left\{x \in  \mathrm{Proj}\left(A \right)\left|\exists y \in  	\mathrm{Proj}\left( C\left( \sX^+\right)\right)\quad \mathfrak{Blowing}\left( y\right) \otimes p_1=\varphi_*\left( x\right)  \otimes p_1\right.\right\}
\eean
For any $\sV\in \mathrm{Proj}^{\mathrm{nat}}\left(A\otimes \K \right)$ there is $\varphi_*\left(\sV \right)  \in \mathrm{Proj}\left(	C\left( \sX^+\right)\otimes  \K \right)$. The $C^*$-algebra 	$C\left( \sX^+\right)\otimes  \K$ is strongly Morita equivalent to 	$C\left( \sX^+\right)$, so $\varphi_*\left(\sV \right)$ uniquely defines $\sV' \in 	\mathrm{Proj}\left( C\left( \sX^+\right)\right)$
\end{empt}
\begin{definition}\label{chern_char_defn}
	Under the above hypothesis for any $\sV\in \mathrm{Proj}^{\mathrm{nat}}\left(A\otimes  \K\right)$ 
	we define  {\it Chern classes} $c_j\left(\sV \right)\in H^{2j}\left(\sX^+, \Z \right)$ of $\sV$ as {Chern classes} of $\sV'\in  \mathrm{Proj}\left( C\left( \sX^+\right)\right)$ (cf. Theorem \ref{chern_class_thm}).
\end{definition}
\begin{remark}
	The search of elements of the Definition \ref{chern_char_defn} can be found from the following commutative diagram
\be\label{chern_char_eqn}
\begin{tikzcd}
\mathbb{M}_n \left( A\right)  \arrow[r, "\varphi_A"] & A \otimes \K \arrow[d, "\varphi"]\\
\mathbb{M}_n\left( 	C\left( \sX^+\right)\right)  \arrow[r, "\varphi_\sX"]	& M\left( A\right) \otimes \K \\
\end{tikzcd}
\ee
\end{remark}
there then for any $j = 0, 2$ there is the pullback (cf. Definition \ref{pullback_defn})
\newline
\newline
\begin{tikzcd}
	K^{\mathrm{nat}}_j \left( A\right) \arrow[d] \arrow[r, "\subset"]
	& K_j\left( A \right)  \arrow[d, "\varphi_2"]\\
	K^j\left(\sX \right)\cong K_j\left(C_0\left(\sX \right)  \right)  \arrow[r, "\varphi_1"]	& K_j\left( M\left( A\right) \right) 
\end{tikzcd}
\\
\\
where $K_j$ and $K^J$ meant $K$-functors of $C^*$-algebras and topological spaces (cf. \cite{blackadar:ko,karoubi:k}). The groups  $K^{\mathrm{nat}}_j \left( A\right)$ are invariants of $A$. Suppose that there is a finitely generated $A^+$-module $P =  \ell^2\left( A^+\right)$ where $e \in \mathbb{M}_\infty \left(A^+ \right) $

 According to 


 Since $K^{\mathrm{nat}}_j \left( A\right)$ is the invariant of $A$ we can define characteristic classes of elements of 	$K^{\mathrm{nat}}_j \left( A\right)$ in cohomology of the space $\sX$.

\begin{remark}\label{k0_rem!!!}!!!!\cite{blackadar:ko}
	There is a homomorphism from $K_{00}(A^+)$ to $K_0(A)$, given by $\left[e\right] \mapsto \left[e\right]- \left[p_n\right]$, where $\pi\left(e \right)$ is a rank $n$ projection in $\mathbb{M}_\infty\left(A \right)$. Composing this with the canonical map from $K_{00}(A)$ to $K_{00}\left(A^+ \right) $ yields a homomorphism $\om_A : K_{00}(A) \to 
	K_0\left(A \right)$.
\end{remark}



\subsubsection{Generalized foliations and inversion of algebraic factorization}
\paragraph*{}	

Let $A$ be a $C^*$-algebra and  let $C_0\left( \sX\right)\subset M\left(A \right)$ be natural Hausdorff blowing-up (cf. Definition \ref{blowing_natural_defn}). Suppose that the equation \eqref{to_spec_eqn} !!! CHECK !!! yields the following diagram of commutative maps
\be\label{gen_foli_eqn}
\begin{tikzcd}
	\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A\right) \arrow[rr] \arrow[rd, "\hat \phi"]&& \sX\arrow[ld, "\phi"]\\
	& \hat A &
\end{tikzcd}
\ee


\begin{definition}\label{generalized_foliation_defn}
	Under the above hypothesis there is the equivalence relation $\sim$ on $\sX$ such that
	\bean
	\forall x', x'' \in \sX \quad x'\sim x'' \quad \Leftrightarrow \quad \phi\left(x' \right)= \phi\left(x'' \right),\\
	\hat{A}\cong \sX/\sim
	\eean 
The decomposition 
$$
\sX = \bigsqcup_{x \in \hat{A}} \phi^{-1}\left(x \right) 
$$
and the diagram \eqref{generalized_foliation_defn}
is a {\it generalized foliation}.
\end{definition}
\begin{remark}
The described above situation is a specialization of algebraic counterpart of geometric quotient (cf. Appendix \ref{quotions_a_sec}) which makes a non Hausdorff spectrum from a Hausdorff space. However the $C^*$-algebra $A$ contains information about both non Hausdorff and Hausdorff spaces. The Hausdorff space $\sX$ can be naturally restored from the $C^*$-algebra $A$. 
\end{remark}

\section{Applications}
\subsection{Fundamental group of commutative $C^*$-algebras}
\paragraph{} If $\sX$ is a connected, locally compact, Hausdorff space then there is a homeomorphism $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(C_0\left(\sX \right)  \right)\cong \sX$. If  $\left(C_0\left(\sX \right), \widetilde{A}, G, \lift \right)$ is a noncommutative covering then there is the given by  \ref{gelfand_map_eqn} continuous map
$$
\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\lift \right): \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\widetilde A \right)\to \sX.
$$
	

	If $B\subset A$  is a hereditary $C^*$-subalgebra evenly covered by $\left(C_0\left(\sX \right), \widetilde{A}, G, \lift \right)$ (cf. Definition \ref{evenly_defn}) then there is a connected open subset $\sU \subset \sX$ with $B \cong \sU$. From the Definition \ref{evenly_defn} it follows that $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\lift \right)^{-1}\left(\sU\right)$ is the disjoint union of homeomorphic to $\sU$ connected open subsets of  $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\widetilde A \right)$, i.e. the map $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\lift \right)$ is a covering. If $\widetilde A$ is not commutative then there is $\widetilde x \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\lift \right)$ with
	$$
\dim \widetilde A / \widetilde x > 1.	
	$$. From the condition (b) of the Definition \ref{fin_pre_defn} it follows that 
	$$
\dim C_0\left( \sX\right) / \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\lift \right)\left( \widetilde x\right) > 1.	
	$$
	It is impossible so $\widetilde A\cong C_0\left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\widetilde A\right) \right)$ is a commutative $C^*$-algebra. Thus there is an 1-1 correspondence between topological and noncommutative coverings of $C_0\left(\sX \right)$. From the Definition \ref{fund_den} that the fundamental group of $C_0\left(\sX \right)$ if it exists is isomorphic to $\pi_1\left( \sX\right)$.
	 \subsection{$C^*$-algebras of compact operators}\label{compact_sec}
\subsubsection{Basic constructions}

	
\paragraph{} If $\H$ is a Hilbert space and $A = \K\left(\H \right)$ then for any  left ideal $L\subset A$ there is a closed $\C$-linear subspace $V_L \subset \H$ such that
\bean
L = \left\{\left.a \in \K\left(\H \right)\right| a \H  \subset V_L\right\}.
\eean
If $L$ is minimal then $V_L$ is a one dimensional space. Any ultrafilter of the $\mathfrak{Lattice}\left(\K\left(\H \right) \right)$ is principal, generated by rank-one element minimal ideal. The set of one-dimensional subspaces of $\H$ is a complex projective space  $\mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)$ (cf. Definition \ref{projective_bundle_defn}), i.e. there is the natural set theoretic bijective map  $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\K\left(\H \right) \right)\cong  \mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)$. The  topology (cf. Definition  of $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\K\left(\H \right)\right) $ contains all sets $\mathbb{P}\left(\H \right) \setminus V$ where $V$ is a linear projective  $\C$-subspace of  $\mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)$ having finite codimension. There identity map yields the  continuous map 
\be\label{gefand_projective_eqn}
\phi_{\H} : \mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)_{\mathfrak{Hausdorff}}\to \mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}\cong \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\K\left(\H \right)\right))_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}
\ee
where $\mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)_{\mathfrak{Hausdorff}} $ is the projective  space with   well known Hausdorff  topology and  $\mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}$ is the same set  having the final with respect to the map  $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\K\left(\H \right) \right)\cong  \mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)$ topology (cf. Definition \ref{top_final_defn}).


\begin{exercise}
Prove that  the given by \eqref{bicommutant_to_eqn} map is a  homeomorphism from  $\mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(\K\left( \sH\right)  \right)$ onto the bicommutant  $ \mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(\K\left(\sH \right)  \right)''$.
\end{exercise}
If
$\dim \H = n < \infty$  then $\H \cong \C^n$, $~A = M_n\left(\C \right)$ and  $\mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)= \mathbb{P}\left( \C^n\right)$. There is the Zariski topology on $ \mathbb{P}\left( \C^n\right)$ such that closed subsets are given by polynomial equations. The closed sets of the Gelfand space are given by linear equations, so the Zariski topology is finer then Gelfand one.
There is a composition of continuous maps
$$
\mathbb{P}\left( \C^n\right)_{\mathfrak{Hausdorff}}\to \mathbb{P}\left( \C^n\right)_{\mathfrak{Zariski}}\to \mathbb{P}\left( \C^n\right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}
$$
where the subscript $_{\mathfrak{Zariski}}$ means the Zariski topology.

\begin{exercise}
	Similarly to the Appendix \ref{loc_const_triv_empt} prove that 
	$$
	\forall r > 0 \quad H^r\left(\mathbb{P}\left( \H\right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}, \mathscr F \right) = 0.
	$$
	for any locally constant sheaf $\mathscr F$ (cf. Definition \ref{constant_presheaf_defn}).
\end{exercise}
\begin{exercise}\label{nontte_exer}
	Similarly to the Theorem \ref{projective_ag_coh_thm} prove that for any  $n \in \N$ and there is $r > 0$  a sheaf $\mathscr F$ with
	$$
	H^r\left(\mathbb{P}\left( \C^n\right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}, \mathscr F \right) \neq 0.
	$$
\end{exercise}
\begin{remark}
	The spectrum of $\K\left(\H \right)$ has the single point but the sheaf cohomology of its Gelfand space $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\K\left(\H \right)  \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}$ are not trivial for $r > 0$ (cf. Exercise \ref{nontte_exer}). 
\end{remark}
\subsubsection{Reconstruction of $C^*$-algebra from the Gelfand space}
\paragraph{}
We already know that the Gelfand space $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left(\C \right)\right)$ (cf. Definition \ref{gelfand_space_defn}) of $\mathbb{M}_n\left(\C \right)$ is $\mathbb{P}\left( \C^{n-1}\right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}$. Consider  $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left(\C \right)\right)$ as an abstract topological space $\sX$ and let us reconstruct the $C^*$-algebra $\mathbb{M}_n\left(\C \right)$. We say that an irreducible closed subset $\sY \subset \sX$ (cf. Definition \ref{top_ireed_defn}) is a \textit{line} if the Dimension (cf. Definition \ref{top_dimension_defn}) of $\sY$ equals to 1.  According to our construction the notion of line is invariant with respect to homeomorphisms, i.e. any homeomorphism of $\sX$ map any line onto a line. From this fact and the fundamental theorem of the projective geometry $\sX$ has the unique structure of complex projective space $\mathbb{P}\left(\C^{n-1} \right)$ modulo automorphism of the field $\C$. The group of automorphisms of   the field $\C$ equals to $\Z_2$. Now one can obtain two $\R$-linearly isomorphic $n$ dimensional complex spaces and to semi-isomorphic $C^*$-algebras $\mathbb{M}_n\left(\C \right)$.

(cf. Appendix \ref{cell_proj_sec}).


\subsection{Gelfand space of continuous trace $C^*$-algebra}
\subsubsection{Basic constructions}

\paragraph{}

		If   $A$  is a {continuous-trace} $C^*$-{algebra} with the spectrum $\sX$ then there is a presheaf  $\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A}$ of sets such that for any open $\sU \subset \sX$  one has
		\be\label{presh_eqn}
		\begin{split}
	\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A}\left(\sU \right) \bydef \\\left\{ C \subset A \text{ is commutative hereditary subalgebra} \left| C \subset ~_\sU A_\sU \text{ cf. \eqref{blowing_hereditary_u_eqn})}\right. \right\};\\
\rho_{\sU\sV} : \mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A}\left(\sU \right)\to \mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A}\left(\sV \right),\\
C \mapsto C \cap ~_\sV A _\sV.
		\end{split}
		\ee
		and let $\mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)$ be the \'espace etal\'e of the presheaf $\mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)$ (cf. Exercise \ref{sheaf_etale_exer}) with the natural local homeomorphism $p_{\mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)} : \mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right) \onto \sX$.

\begin{lemma}\label{ctr_gelfand_lem}
	If $A$ is a {continuous-trace} $C^*$-{algebra} then there is the natural bijective set theoretic map $\phi_{\mathscr P}:\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right) \cong \mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)$  with the following commutative diagram
	\newline
	\begin{tikzcd}
	\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right)		 \arrow[rr, "\cong"]\arrow[rd, "\hat \phi"]  & ~ & \mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right) \arrow[ld, "p_{\mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)}" ]\\
		& \sX &
	\end{tikzcd}
\end{lemma}	
\begin{proof}
 Let 
\bean
\mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)_x \bydef \left\{\left.\eta \in \mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)\right| 	p_{\mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A}  \right)}\left(\eta \right) = x\right\},\\
\mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)_\xi =  \left\{\left.\zeta \in \mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)_x\right| \forall B \in \xi \quad  \exists  C \subset B\quad \zeta = C_x  \right\}
\eean
where $C$ is a commutative $C^*$-subalgebra which represents $\zeta$ and $C_x$ is the germ of $C$ at $x$ (cf. Definition \ref{sheaf_stalk_defn}). If $\mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)_\xi$ contains more than one element and $\zeta \in \mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)_\xi$ then the  filter of hereditary $C^*$-subalgebras
\bean
\left\{B \subset A \left| \exists  C \subset B \quad \zeta = C_x \right.\right\}
\eean 
exceeds $\xi$. It is impossible since $\xi$ is an ultrafilter. If $C', C''\subset \xi$ are two commutative $C^*$-algebras  then one has
$$
\forall f \in C_0\left(\sX \right) \quad f\left(x \right)\neq 0 \quad\left(  \mathfrak {Blowing}_{\sX-A }(f) C'\right) \cap \left( \mathfrak {Blowing}_{\sX-A }(f) C''\right)  \neq \{0\}.
$$
It is possible if and only if and only if $C'_x = C''_x$, so there is the natural  map $\phi_{\mathscr P} :\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right) \cong \mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)$. On the other hand if $\zeta \in \mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)$ and 
$$
\xi \bydef \left\{ B \in A \left| \exists C \subset B \quad C_x = \zeta\right.\right\}
$$
then $\phi_{\mathscr P}\left(\xi \right) = \zeta$, i.e. the map $\phi_{\mathscr P}$ is bijective.
\end{proof}
\begin{remark}
Denote by $\mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)_{\mathfrak{Etale}}$ the set $\mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)$ supplied with the smallest topology such that the map $\mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)_{\mathfrak{Etale}}\to \sX$ is continuous. If $\mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}$ is the topological space such that the bijective map $\mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}\cong \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right)$ is  homeomorphism then since the map $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right)\to \sX$ is continuous the topology of $\mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}$ is finer than $\mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)_{\mathfrak{Etale}}$ one. 
\end{remark}
\begin{corollary}\label{ctr_bic_cor}
	If $A$ is a {continuous-trace} $C^*$-{algebra} then for any element $\xi \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right)$ of the Gelfand space (cf. Definition \ref{gelfand_space_defn})	the bicommutant of $\xi''$ (cf. Definition \ref{bicommutant_defn}) is a proper maximal closed left ideal. 
\end{corollary}
\begin{proof}
From the Lemma \ref{ctr_gelfand_lem} it follows that $\xi$ corresponds to $C_{x_\xi} \in \mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)$ where $x_\xi \bydef \hat \phi\left( \xi\right)$ and  $C \subset A$ is a  representative of the element of $ \mathrm{Sp\acute{e}}\left(\mathscr P_{\sX\text{-}A} \right)$. If $V_\xi \bydef \rep_{x_\xi}\left(C \right) \H_{x_\xi}$ then then the closed left ideal
\bean
L_\xi \bydef \left\{a \in A \left| \rep_{x_\xi}\left(a \right) \H_{x_\xi}\perp V_\xi\right.\right\}
\eean
is proper and maximal. There is an open neighborhood $\sV$ of $x_\xi$ and $c \in C$ such that
$$
\forall x \in \sV \quad \left\|\rep_x\left(c \right)  \right\| = 1.
$$
If $a \in L_\xi$,  $~~a' \bydef c a c$ and $a''\bydef a - a'$ then  there is $f \in C_c \left(\sX \right)_+$ such that
\bean
f\left( x_\xi\right) = 0,\\
\forall x \in \sV \quad f\left(x \right) = \left\|\rep_x\left(a' \right)  \right\|, \quad c a'' c = 0.
\eean
there is a basis $\left\{\sU\right\}$ of neighborhoods of $x_\xi$  such that $\sU \subset \sV$ for any $\sU \in  \left\{\sU\right\}$. One can find a family $\left\{f_\sU\right\}_{\sU \in \left\{\sU\right\}}$
such that $f_\sU \left(\sU \right)= \{0\}$ and there is the uniform limit
$$
f = \lim_{\sU \in  \left\{\sU\right\}} f_\sU.
$$
If $C_\sU \bydef C \cap~_\sU A _\sU$ and 
  $L_\sU$ is a closed left ideal with $C_\sU= L_\sU \cap L^*_\sU$ (cf. Lemma \ref{hered_ideal_lem}), $a_\sU \bydef a'' = f_\sU a'$ then
\bean
L_\sU a_\sU^* = 0 \quad \Rightarrow\quad a_\sU \in L^\perp_\sU,\\
a = \lim_{\sU \in  \left\{\sU\right\}} a_\sU
\eean
From the above equations it turns out that $L_\xi$ is a subset of the $C^*$-norm closure of the union $\bigcup_{\sU \in  \left\{\sU\right\}}L_\sU$. Using this fact one can proof that $\xi'' = L_\xi$.
\end{proof}
\begin{remark}\label{ctr_bic_rem}
From the proof of the Corollary it follows that any element of the bicommutant $ \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right)''$ of the Gelfand space  $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right)$ uniquely depends on the pair $\left( x_\xi, V_\xi\right)$. Since $V_\xi \subset \H_{x_\xi}$ is one-dimensional subspace any  element of $ \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right)''$ uniquely depends of the pair $\left( x_\xi, y_\xi\right)$ where $y_\xi \in \mathbb{P}\left(\H_{x_\xi} \right)$ and $\mathbb{P}\left(\H_{x_\xi} \right)$ is the projective space (cf. Definition \ref{projective_bundle_defn}).
\end{remark}
\begin{lemma}
If $\sX$ is a locally compact Hausdorff space and $A \bydef C_0\left( \sX\right) \otimes \K\left( \sH\right)$ then there is the natural homeomorphism
\be\label{ctr_prod_eqn}
\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right)''\cong \sX \times \mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}
\ee
where $\mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}$ isn given by \eqref{gefand_projective_eqn} projective space with Gelfand topology.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
The Corollary \ref{ctr_bic_cor} and the Remark \ref{ctr_bic_rem} naturally  yield a given by \eqref{ctr_prod_eqn} bijective map. One should prove that the map is a homeomorphism. Clearly an open subset of $\sX \times \mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}$ is open in  $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right)''$. Let $\left(x_\xi, y_\xi \right)$ be a pair which yields a point of both $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right)''$ and $\sX \times \mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}$, and let $\sU\subset $
\end{proof}

\begin{proof}

	Here we use the  construction \ref{topology_base_herd_empt}.
If $\xi \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right)$ then there 
from the  Lemma  \ref{ctr_g_lem} it follows that there is a pair $\left(x_\xi, y_\xi \right)$ such that for any $B \in \xi$ the one-dimensional subspace
$$
\rep_{x_\xi} \left(L\right)\sH_{x_\xi}\subset  \sH_{x_\xi}
$$ 
corresponds to $y_\xi \in \mathbb{P}\left(\H_x \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}$.
\end{proof}


\subsubsection{Comparison with the bundle space} 
\paragraph*{}
Suppose that $A$ is the given by the Proposition \ref{ctr_bundle_prop}  locally trivial   fibre bundle $\F$ with fibre $\K = \K\left(\H \right)$. There is a subbundle $\E \subset \F$ such that fibers of $\E$ are  rank-one positive operators. It gives a locally trivial bundle $\mathbb{P}\left(\E \right)\xrightarrow{\phi_\E} \sX$ such that any fibre of $\phi_\E$ is a complex projective space $\mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)$. From the Lemma \ref{ctr_g_lem} it follows that there is a set theoretic bijective map
\bean
\phi_C: \mathbb{P}\left(\E \right)\cong  \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)''.
\eean     
There is the initial with respect to $\phi_C$ on  topology on $\mathbb{P}\left(\E \right)$ (cf, Definition \ref{top_init_defn}), we denote                                                   corresponding space by $\mathbb{P}\left(\E \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}$. The bijective map $\phi_C$ we denote by 
\be\label{ctr_bundle_eqn}
\begin{split}
\mathbb{P}\left(\E \right)_{\mathfrak{Hausdorff}}\xrightarrow{\phi)_{\mathbb{P}\left( \E\right) }} \mathbb{P}\left(\E \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}
\end{split}
\ee
where $\mathbb{P}\left(\E \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}$ and $\mathbb{P}\left(\E \right)_{\mathfrak{Hausdorff}}$, is the set $\mathbb{P}\left(\E \right)$ having Gelfand and well known Hausdorff topology. 

\begin{empt}\label{ctr_bundle_empt}

If  $F$ be an Abelian group then from the Proposition \ref{spectral_sequence_prop} it follows that there are the natural homomorphisms
\be\label{h_ctr_eqn}
\begin{split}
H^*\left(\phi_{\mathbb{P}\left( \E\right)} \right) :  H^*\left( \mathbb{P}\left(\E \right)_{\mathfrak{Hausdorff}}, F \right) \cong  H^* \left( \mathbb{P}\left(\E \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}},  F\right)
\end{split}
\ee
