		;
	\end{tikzpicture}
	\\
	in which the rows are exact, excepting the first, as just shown and the
	columns are exact, excepting the first, by \ref{top_cech_ree_thm}. A diagram chase
	shows that the homology of the first (nontrivial) row is isomorphic to that
	of the first column.
\end{proof}	
	\begin{empt}
	If $f: \sX\to\sY$ is a continuous map  $\mathscr U = \left\{\sU_\iota\right\}_{\iota} \in I$ is a covering of $\sY$ (cf. Definition \ref{pretopology_defn}    and Example \ref{top_gro_exm}) then a family $f^{-1}\left(\mathscr U \right) \bydef \left\{f^{-1}\left( \sU_\iota\right) \right\}_{\iota} \in I$ is a covering of $\sX$. Let $F$ be a Abelian group, and let $F_\sX$, $F_\sY$ be a corresponding constant presheaves (cf. Definition \ref{constant_presheaf_defn}) on $\sX$ and $\sY$.  Following equation
	\be\label{top_cech_eqn}
	C^r\left( \mathscr U,  F_\sY\right)\bydef \prod_{\left(\iota_0,.... \iota_r\right) \in I^{r+1}}  F_\sY\left(\sU_{\iota_0,.... \iota_r} \right)\quad \text{where} \quad \sU_{\iota_0,.... \iota_r} \bydef \sU_{\iota_0}\cap...\cap \sU_{\iota_r}. 
	\ee
	is a specialization of \eqref{cech_eqn} one (cf. Example ???? \ref{top_gro_exm}). For any $\left(\iota_0,.... \iota_r\right) \in I^{r+1}$ one has an isomorphism
	$$
	F_\sY\left(\sU_{\iota_0,.... \iota_r} \right)\cong F_\sX\left(f^{-1}\left( \sU_{\iota_0,.... \iota_r} \right)\right) \cong F.
	$$
	Above isomorphisms yield an isomorphism
	$$
	C^r\left( \mathscr U, F_\sY\right)\xrightarrow{\approx} C^r\left( f^{-1}\left( \mathscr U\right) , F_\sX\right)
	$$
	So there is an isomorphism
	$$
	\varinjlim_{\mathscr U}\check{H}^r\left( \mathscr U, F_\sY\right)\xrightarrow{\approx}\varinjlim_{\mathscr U}\check{H}^r\left(f^{-1}\left(  \mathscr U\right) , F_\sX\right).
	$$
	On the other hand from   \eqref{chech_eqn}  it follows that there are homomorphisms
	\bean
	\check{H}^r\left(f^{-1}\left(  \mathscr U\right) , F_\sX\right)\to \check{H}^r\left(\sX , F_\sX\right),\\
	\varinjlim_{\mathscr U} \check{H}^r\left(f^{-1}\left(  \mathscr U\right), F_\sX\right)\to \check{H}^r\left(\sX , F_\sX\right)
	\eean
	so one has a homomorphism
	$$
	\varinjlim_{\mathscr U} \check{H}^r\left(  \mathscr U, F_\sY\right)\to \check{H}^r\left(\sX , F_\sX\right)
	$$
	and applying \eqref{chech_eqn} one can obtain a natural homomorphism
	$$
	\check{H}^r\left(f\right):\check{H}^r\left(\sY, F_\sY \right)\to \check{H}^r\left(\sX, F_\sX \right)\quad r \ge 0.
	$$
	The details of the construction of the homomorphism $\check{H}^r\left(f\right)$  are explained in \cite{eust}. Using the Notation \ref{constant_presheaf_defn} one has homomorphisms
	\be\label{cech_hom_eqn}
	\begin{split}
		\check{H}^r\left(f\right):\check{H}^r\left(\sY, F \right)\to \check{H}^r\left(\sX, F \right)\quad r \ge 0,\\
		\check{H}^\bullet\left(f\right):\check{H}^\bullet\left(\sY, F \right)\to \check{H}^\bullet\left(\sX, F \right).
	\end{split}
	\ee
	If both $\sX \xrightarrow{f}\sY$ and $\sY \xrightarrow{g}\sZ$ are continuous maps then from this construction it turns out that
	\be\label{cech_hom_comp_eqn}
	\begin{split}
		\check{H}^\bullet\left(g\circ f\right)= \check{H}^\bullet\left( f\right)\circ \check{H}^\bullet\left(g\right):\check{H}^\bullet\left(\sZ, F \right)\to \check{H}^\bullet\left(\sX, F \right)
	\end{split}
	\ee
	
\end{empt}
			\subsection{Nonabelian cohomology}
\paragraph{} Here I follow to \cite{grothendieck:sheaf_noabelian}.  Let $\sX$ be a topological space, and let $\G$ be a sheaf of groups (not necessary Abelian) on $\sX$. Let $\mathscr U \bydef \left\{\sU_\iota\right\}_{\iota \in I}$ be an open covering of $\sX$/ We write
$
\sU_{\iota_0, ..., \iota_{p}}\bydef \sU_{\iota_0} \cap ...\cap \sU_{\iota_p}	
$ for any $\left(\iota_0, ..., \iota_p\right)\in I^{p+1}$.
\begin{definition}\label{nonab_coh_defn}
	We define the \textit{group of }$p$-\textit{cochains of the covering } $\mathscr U$ \textit{with coefficients in the sheaf of groups } $\G$ as the product group
	$$
	C^p\left(\mathscr U , \G \right) \bydef	\prod_{I^p }H^0\left(\sU_{\iota_0, ..., \iota_{p}}, \G \right). 
	$$ A 1-cochain $\left(g_{\iota, j} \right)$ is called a  1 - \textit{cocycle} if it satisfies  the conditions
	\be\label{nonab_coh_eqn}
	\sU_{\iota, j, k}\neq \emptyset \quad \Rightarrow  \quad  g_{\iota, k} = g_{\iota, j}g_{j,k}.
	\ee
	(We recall that for any open $\sU\subset \sX$,  $~H^0\left(\sU, \G \right)$ is the group of sections of $\G$ on $\sU$). Thus an element of $C^P\left( \mathscr U, \G\right)$ is an arbitrary family $\left\{g_{\iota_0}, ..., g_{\iota_p}\right\} $ of sections of $\G$ on the intersection $\sU_{\iota_0, ..., \iota_{p}}$.
	The set of 1-cocycles in $C^1\left( \mathscr U, \G\right)$ (which set in general is not a subgroup) however is denoted by  $Z^1\left( \mathscr U, \G\right)$,
\end{definition}
Let $g^0 = \left\{g_\iota\right\}\in C^0\left( \mathscr U, \G\right)$, $~g^1 = \left\{g_{\iota, j}\right\}\in C^1\left( \mathscr U, \G\right)$, we define an element $D\left( g^0\right).g^1 \in Z^1\left( \mathscr U, \G\right)$ by
\be\label{nonab_perm_eqn}
\left( D\left( g^0\right).g^1\right)_{\iota, j}
\bydef  g_\iota g_{\iota, j} g^{-1}_j.
\ee  
With this definition, $D$ is a representation of the group $C^0\left( \mathscr U, \G\right)$ by permutations of the set $C^1\left( \mathscr U, \G\right)$; it is moreover trivial that $Z^1\left( \mathscr U, \G\right)$ is stable under the operations of $C^0\left( \mathscr U, \G\right)$. Denote by
\be\label{nonab_coh_q_eqn}
H^1\left( \mathscr U, \G\right) \bydef Z^1\left( \mathscr U, \G\right)/D\left( C^0\left( \mathscr U, \G\right)\right) 
\ee
If $\mathscr V$ is a refinement of the covering $\mathscr U$ then similarly to \eqref{cech_refi_eqn} for any $p$ there is a natural homomorphism
$$
C^p\left( \mathscr U, \G\right) \to C^p\left( \mathscr V, \G\right) .
$$
It is proven in \cite{grothendieck:sheaf_noabelian} that the homomorphism of chains yields a map  $C^p\left( \mathscr U, \G\right) \to C^p\left( \mathscr V, \G\right)$.

\begin{definition}\label{nonab_coh_den}\cite{grothendieck:sheaf_noabelian}
	Let $\G$ be a bundle of groups. We denote by 
	\be
	H^1\left( \sX, \G\right)\bydef \varinjlim_{\mathscr U}H^1\left( \mathscr U, \G\right)
	\ee
	and call the \textit{first cohomology set of } $\sX$ \textit{ with coefficients in } $\G$.
	An element of this inductive limit is class of elements in the union of sets $H^1\left( \mathscr U, \G\right)$, an element in $H^1\left( \mathscr U, \G\right)$ being equivalent to an element in $H^1\left( \mathscr V, \G\right)$ if and only if for a suitable common refinement $\mathscr W$ of $\mathscr U$ and $\mathscr V$, the canonical image of these elements in  $H^1\left( \mathscr U, \G\right)$ are same.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}\cite{bryl:loop}
	%4.1.2. Proposition. 
	Let $G$ be a Lie group, and let $\underline{G}$ be the sheaf of germs 
	of continuous $G$-valued functions. Then $H^1\left(M,  \underline{G}\right) $  identifies naturally, as a 
	pointed set, with the set of isomorphism classes of principal $G$-bundles over 
	$M$.
\end{proposition}
\begin{theorem}\label{nc_coh_exact_thm}\cite{bryl:loop}
%4.1.3. Theorem. [Grl] [Gr2]
If $1\hookto A \hookto B\onto C \onto 1$ is an exact 
sequence of sheaves of groups on a space $M$, there is an exact sequence of 
pointed sets 
\be
\begin{split}
1 \hookto H^0\left(M, A \right) \hookto H^0\left(M, B \right) \to H^0\left(M, C \right) \xrightarrow{\dl_0}  H^1\left(M, A \right) \to\\ \to H^1\left(M, B \right) \to H^1\left(M, C \right).
\end{split}
\ee
\end{theorem}
\begin{empt}
An important case of an exact sequence $1\hookto A \hookto B\onto C \onto 1$ of 
sheaves of groups is obtained from a sheaf of $\C$-algebras $R$ over $M$. Then 
one has the exact sequence 
\be\label{z_spec_eqn}
1 \hookto Z(R)^* \hookto R^* \onto R^*/Z(R)^* \onto 1, 
\ee
where $Z(R)$ is the center of $R$, and $R^*$ denotes the sheaf of groups of invertible elements in $R$. A special feature of the exact sequence \eqref{z_spec_eqn} is that the 
first sheaf of groups is central in the middle one. Such an exact sequence is 
called {\it central}. In that case, one can continue the exact sequence of Theorem 
\ref{nc_coh_exact_thm} one step to the right.
\end{empt}
\begin{theorem}\label{nc_coh_exact_central_thm}\cite{bryl:loop}
	%4.1.4 Theorem. [Grl] [Gr2]
	In the situation of Theorem \ref{nc_coh_exact_thm}, assume furthermore 
	that $A$ is central in $B$. Then one has the exact sequence of pointed sets 
\be\label{nc_coh_exact_central_eqn}
\begin{split}
	1 \hookto H^0\left(M, A \right) \hookto H^0\left(M, B \right) \to H^0\left(M, C \right) \xrightarrow{\dl_0}  H^1\left(M, A \right) \to\\ \to H^1\left(M, B \right) \to H^1\left(M, C \right) \xrightarrow{\dl_1}  H^2\left(M, A \right).
\end{split}
\ee
Here $H^1\left(M, C \right) \xrightarrow{\dl_1}  H^2\left(M, A \right)$ is defined as follows. Let $c_{jk}$ be a \v{C}ech	1-cocycle of the open covering $\left\{\sU_j \right\}$ with values in $C$,such that $c_{jk}= p\left(b_{jk} \right)$ 
	for $b_{jk} \in \Ga \left(\sU_{jk}, B\right)$ . Then $a_{jkl} \bydef b_{jl}^{-1}b_{jk}b_{kl}$ gives a \v{C}ech 2-cocycle $\underline{a}$ with 
	values in $A$. $\dl_1$ then maps the cohomology class of $\underline{c}$ to that of $\underline{a}$. 

\end{theorem}
Note that since $A$ is sheaf of Abelian groups, $ H^2\left(M, A \right)$ is defined.

\subsection{Relative cohomology}
\paragraph*{} Here I follow to \cite{bredon:sheaf}
Let $j : \hookto \sX$ and let $\Phi$ be a family of supports on $\sX$. For any sheaf $\mathscr A$ on $\sX$ we have the natural $j$-cohomomorphism %(see Section 8)
\bean
\mathscr C^*\left(\sX; \mathscr A\right) \to C^*\left(A; \mathscr A|A\right)
\eean
Equivalently, we have the homomorphism
\bean
\mathscr C\left(\sX; \mathscr A\right) 
j^*: \mathscr C^*\left(\sX; \mathscr A\right) \to j^*C^*\left(A; \mathscr A|A\right)
\eean
of sheaves on $\sX$.
In order to define relative cohomology, we shall show that $j^*$ is surjective
and has a flabby kernel. We introduce the notation
\bean
\ker j^* \bydef  \mathscr C^*\left(\sX, A ;\mathscr A\right),\\
C^*_\Phi\left(\sX, A; \mathscr A\right)\bydef \Ga_\Phi\left( C^*\left(\sX; A \mathscr A\right)\right) 
\eean
and
\bean
H^*_\Phi \left(\sX, A; \mathscr A\right) \bydef H^*\left( C^*_\Phi\left(\sX, A; \mathscr A\right)\right) 
\eean 
Since $\ker j^*$ is flabby and since $\G_\Phi\left(j \mathscr B \right) = \Ga_{\Phi \cap A}\left(\mathscr B \right)$  % by I-Exercise 8, we will
obtain the induced short exact sequence
\bean
0 \hookto C^*_\Phi\left(\sX, A;\mathscr A  \right) \hookto C^*_\Phi\left(\sX;\mathscr A  \right)\onto C^*_\Phi\left(A;\mathscr A | A \right)\onto 0
\eean
and hence the long exact cohomology sequence
\be 
... \to  H^p_\Phi\left(\sX, A;\mathscr A  \right) \to H^p_\Phi\left(A;\mathscr A  \right)\to  H^{p+1}_\Phi\left(A;\mathscr A | A \right)\to ...
\ee

\subsection{Descent of sheaves}
\paragraph*{} Here I follow to \cite{bryl:loop}. There is an alternative description of sheaves based on the notion of local homeomorphisms (cf. Definition \ref{local_homeo_defn}). Instead of an 
open subset of $\sX$, we will more generally consider a continuous mapping 
$f: \sX \to \sY$ of some space $\sX$ into $\sY$ (in the terminology of Grothendieck, this 
is called a "space over $\sX$"). If $\mathscr A$ is sheaf over $\sX$ them there is an inverse image sheaf $f^{-1}\mathscr A$ (cf. Definition \ref{sheaf_inv_im_defn}) over $\sY$. Then we can define a 
set $\mathscr A\left(\sY \to \sX \right)$  (or simply $A\left( \sY\right)$ ) to be the set $\Ga\left(\sY, f^{-1} \mathscr A\right)$  of global sections 
of the pull-back sheaf over $\sY$. Now let $g : \sZ \to \sX$ be another continuous 
mapping. Assume there exists a, continuous mapping $h : \sZ \to \sY$ such that 
$g = f\circ h$. Then we have a pull-back map $h^*:  \mathscr A\left(\sY \xrightarrow{f} \sX \right)\to \mathscr A\left(\sX \xrightarrow{g} \sX \right)$.

Note that, given an open covering $\left\{\sU_j\right\}$ of the open set $\sV \subset \sX$ as above, we have a continuous mapping $f: \sY \bydef \coprod_j \to \sX$, where the restriction of $f$ to each $\sU_j$ is the inclusion map, yielding $\mathscr A\left(\sY \xrightarrow{f} \sX \right)\bydef \prod_{j \in J} \mathscr A\left( \sU_j\right)$. The glueing condition involves all the intersections $\sU{jk}$, which are all open subsets of the space $\sY \times_\sX \sY$, the fiber product of $f: \sY \to \sX$ with itself. The 
fiber product is the set of $\left(y_1, y_2 \right)\in \sY \times \sY$  such that $f\left( y_1\right)=f\left( y_2\right)$ There 
are two projection maps $p_1, p_2: \sY \times_\sX  \sY$ such that $p_j\left(y_1, y_2 \right)= y_j$ . However there is only one mapping $\sY \times_\sX \times \sY\to \sX$, given by $g\left(y1, y2 \right) = f\left(y_1 \right)= f\left(y_2 \right)$. When $\sY = \coprod_j \sU_j$ is the disjoint union of 
the $\sU_j$ and $f : \sY \to \sX$ is the (local) inclusion, then $\sY \times_\sX  \sY$ is the disjoint union of the $\sU_j \times_\sX  \sU_k=\sU_{jk}$. The restriction of $p_1$ to $\sU_{jk}$ is the inclusion 
of $\sU{jk}$ into the component $\sU_j$ of $\sY$, and the restriction of $p_2$ to $\sU_{jk}$ is the inclusion of $\sU{jk}$ into $\sU_k$. 

The glueing property therefore means that the following sequence
\be\label{f_ex_eqn} 
F\left(\sV \right)\xrightarrow{f^{-1}} F \left( \sY\right) \substack{ \xrightarrow{p_1^{-1}}\\\xrightarrow[p_2^{-1}]{}} F\left(\sY\times_\sX \sY \right) 
\ee 
is an exact sequence of sets, whenever $\sV$ is an open subset of $\sX$, and $\sY = \coprod_j \sU_j$, for $\left\{\sU_j\right\}$ an open covering of $\sV$. What this means is that $f^{-1}$ induces a bijection between $F\left(\sV \right)$ and the kernel $\ker\left( p_1, p_2\right)$  of the pair $\left( p_1, p_2\right)$, 
i.e., the set of elements $s\in F\left(\sY \right)$  such that $p_1^{-1}\left( s\right) = p_2^{-1}\left( s\right)$  Of course $f^{-1}$ induces a mapping from $f\left(\sY \right)$  to this kernel; surjectivity of the map implies 	the existence of a "glued together" section, and injectivity means that the glued together section is unique. Such a formulation of the glueing property 	is more elegant and compact, and it can be generalized to mappings other 	than the inclusion of a disjoint union of open sets. 
	
Note that the composition of two local homeomorphisms (cf. Definition \ref{local_homeo_defn}) is again one, that the inclusion of a disjoint union of open sets is a local homeomorphism, and that a covering map is also a local homeomorphism (in fact, a very special one). If $f: \sY \to \sX$ is a local homeomorphism, and $g : \sZ \to \sX$ is any continuous map, the map $\sZ \times_\sX \to \sZ$ is again a local homeomorphism. Given a local homeomorphism $f: \sY \to \sX$, with $\sX$ is a smooth manifold, $\sY$ acquires the structure of a smooth manifold, with respect to which $f$ is a local diffeomorphism. 
\begin{proposition}\cite{bryl:loop}
%5.1.2. Proposition. 
If $\mathscr A$ is a sheaf on $\sX$, for every open set $\sV$ of $\sV$ and 
any surjective local homeomorphism $f: \sY \to \sV$, the sequence of sets \eqref{f_ex_eqn} 
is exact. 
\end{proposition}
Thus we get a new definition of a sheaf of sets $\mathscr A$ on $\sX$. In the 
new definition, such a sheaf $\mathscr A$ will associate to any local homeomorphism 
$f: \sY \to \sX$  a set $\mathscr A\left( \sY \to \sX\right) $, and to a diagram $\sZ \xrightarrow{g}\sY \xrightarrow{f}\sX$ of local homeomorphisms, a pull-back map $g^{-1} : \mathscr A\left(\sY \to \sX \right)$. The pull-back map should be compatible with the composition of such diagrams, so that if we have local homeomorphisms $\mathcal W \xrightarrow[]{h}\sZ \xrightarrow[]{g}\sY\xrightarrow[]{p}\sX$, the 	pull-back map $\left( gh\right)^{-1}: \mathscr A\left(\sY \xrightarrow{f} \sX \right)\to \mathscr A\left(\mathcal W \xrightarrow{fgh} \sX \right)$ is the composite of $g^{-1} : \mathscr A\left(\sY \xrightarrow{f} \sX \right)$ and of $h^{-1}:\mathscr A\left(\sY \xrightarrow{f} \sX \right)$. 					Then $\mathscr A$ is a sheaf if and only if, for any open set $\sV$ of $\sX$ and every surjective 	local homeomorphism $f: \sY \to \sV$, the sequence of sets \eqref{f_ex_eqn} is exact. 

Note that, given a space $\sX$, we have a category $\mathscr C_\sX$, whose objects are the local homeomorphisms $\sX$, and such that a morphism from  $\sZ \to \sX$ 
to $\sY \to \sX$ is a commutative diagram 
\be\label{f_sheaf_eqn}
		\begin{tikzcd}
\sZ	 \arrow[rr, "g"]\arrow[rd, "h"]  & ~ & \sY \arrow[ld, , "f"]\\
	& \sX &
\end{tikzcd}
\ee
where $g$ is a local homeomorphism. A sheaf of sets $\mathscr F$ on $\sX$ gives rise to a contravariant functor from $\mathscr C_\sX$ to the category $Sets$ of sets. The category $\mathscr C_\sX$ % gives a nice interpretation of the notion of a refinement $\left\{\sV_j\right\}_{j \in J}$ of an open covering $\left\{\sU_\iota right\}_{\iota \in I}$ of $\sX$. It means that there 
	exists a mapping $f " J \to I$ such that $\sV_j \subset \sU_{f\left( j\right) }$  for all $j \in J$. Observe that such a mapping gives rise to a local homeomorphism $h : \coprod_{j\in J}\sV_j\to  \coprod_{\iota\in I}\sU_\iota$.
	which makes the following diagram commute 
\be\label{f_sheaf_ij_eqn}
\begin{tikzcd}
	\coprod_{j\in J}\sV_j	 \arrow[rr, "g"]\arrow[rd, "h"]  & ~ & 	\coprod_{\iota\in I}\sU_\iota \arrow[ld, , "f"]\\
	& \sX &
\end{tikzcd}
\ee	

We now come to the glueing property. If $f: \sY \to \sX$ is a surjective local 
	homeomorphism, one can obtain a section of a sheaf $\mathscr A$ over $\sX$ from a section $s$ of $\mathscr A$ over $f: \sY \to \sX$ satisfying the glueing condition $p_1^{-1}\left(s \right) = p_2^{-1}\left(s \right)$ in 
	$\mathscr A\left(\sY \times_\sX \sY \right)$. We apply this to morphisms of sheaves. Given 	sheaves $\mathscr A$ and $\mathscr B$ over $\sX$, a morphism of sheaves $\phi: \mathscr A\to \mathscr B$ consists of 	mappings $\mathscr A\left(\sU \right)\to \mathscr B\left(\sU \right) $  for every open set $\sU$ such that, for $\sV \subset \sU$, we have a commutative diagram 

\bean
\begin{tikzcd}
	\mathscr A\left(\sU \right)\arrow[d, "\rho_{\sV, \sU}"] \arrow[r, "\phi_\sU"]& \mathscr B\left(\sU \right)\arrow[d, "\rho_{\sV, \sU}"]\\
	\mathscr A\left(\sV \right) \arrow[r, "\phi_\sU"]& \mathscr B\left(\sV \right)
\end{tikzcd}
\eean
Similarly we have the notion of morphism of sheaves of groups. If $\mathscr A$ and 
$\mathscr A$ are two sheaves of groups over $\sX$, the set of morphisms from $\mathscr A$ to $\mathscr B$ is denoted by $\Hom_\sX(A, B)$. For every open set $\sU$ of $\sX$, there is a natural restriction map $\Hom_\sX (A,B) \to \Hom_\sU\left(A|_\sU, B_\sU \right)$. Thus we have a presheaf $\sU \mapsto Hom_\sU\left(A|_\sU, B_\sU \right)$ 
, which is denoted by $\mathcal{Hom}\left(\mathscr A. \mathscr B \right)$. It is easy to see that this is a sheaf on $\sX$. Given a local homeomorphism $f: \sY \to \sX$, the value of the sheaf $\mathcal{Hom}\left(\mathscr A, \mathscr B \right)$ on $f$ is $\mathcal{Hom}_\sY\left(f^{-1}\mathscr A, f^{-1}\mathscr B \right)$. The fact that 	Hom(A, B) is a sheaf means that, given an open set $\sV$ and a surjective 
	local homeomorphism $f: \sY \to \sV$, a morphism $\phi: \mathscr A|_\sV \to B|_{\sV}$ of sheaves of 	groups over $\sX$ is the same as a morphism $\psi : f^{-1} \mathscr A \to f^{-1} \mathscr B$ of the pull-back 	sheaves on $\sY$ such that we have $p_1^{-1}\left( \psi\right) = p_2^{-1}\left( \psi\right)$ as morphisms of sheaves on $\sY \times_\sX \sY$.
	\begin{remark}\label{sheaf_desc_rem}\cite{bryl:loop}
The above situation  is usually phrased by saying that morphisms of sheaves 
satisfy {\it descent} with respect to local homeomorphisms. 
	\end{remark}




\section{Dixmier Douady theory}
\subsection{Dixmier Douady theory of spaces}
	\paragraph*{} Here I follow to \cite{bryl:loop}
	If $M$ is a manifold then $H^2\left(M, \Z \right)$ is the group of isomorphism  classes of line bundles over $M$
	Given a paracompact space $M$, we wish to describe bundles over $M$ which 
	represent classes in $H^3\left(M, \Z \right)$  Actually it is more convenient to work with 
	the isomorphic group $H^3\left(M, \Z \left( 1\right) \right)$, where $\Z\left( 1\right)\bydef 2\pi\sqrt{-1} \cdot \Z$. First, let us 	use the exponential exact sequence of sheaves $0\to\Z\left(1 \right)\to \underline{\C}_M\xrightarrow{\exp}\underline{\C}^*_M\to 0$. Using the exact sequence of cohomology one can identify $H^3\left( M,\Z\left(1\right)\right) $  and  $H^2\left( M,\underline{\C}^*_M\right) $ 
Here we  $\underline{\C}^*_M$ is used to denote the sheaf of continuous $\C^*$-valued functions on open sets of $M$. We will 
	need degree 1 \v{C}ech cohomology with values in a sheaf of nonabelian groups
	We wish to apply the Theorem \ref{nc_coh_exact_central_eqn}  to the exact sequence \eqref{nc_coh_exact_central_eqn} in the case 
	of a suitable sheaf of algebras $R$. As we are interested in the cohomology 
	group $H^2\left(M, \underline{\C}^*_M \right)$, we want the center of $R$ to be the sheaf $\underline{\C}^*_M$. Let us 
	take the sheaf of algebras $R$ to be the sheaf $\underline L_M$ of continuous functions 
	with values in some Banach algebra $L$, with center equal to $\C$. The best 
	choice will turn out to be the algebra $L = \L\left(E \right)$ of bounded operators in a 
	separable Hilbert space $E$; the norm is the sup-norm of an operator. It is 
	well-known (and easy to see) that the center of $L$ is equal to $\C$. The quotient 
	Lie group $L^*/\C^*$ identifies with the Lie group $G = Aut\left( \K\right)$  of continuous 
	algebra automorphisms of the Banach algebra K of compact operators of $E$. 
	In other words, one has an exact sequence of Lie groups 
	\be\label{ctr_seq_eqn}
1 \hookto C^* \hookto L^* \cong Aut\left(E \right)\onto G = Aut\left(\K \right) \onto 1.  
\ee
			Since the mapping $Aut\left(E \right)\onto G$  is a principal $\C^*$-fibration, one has an exact 
			sequence of sheaves of continuous functions with values in \eqref{ctr_seq_eqn}, to wit: 
	\be
	\{1\} \hookto \underline{C}^*_M \hookto\underline{L}^*_M \onto\underline{G}_M\onto \{1\}.
	\ee
			The following result is the basic reason behind the choice of this Banach 
			algebra $L$. 
			\begin{proposition}\cite{bryl:loop}
%4.1.5. Proposition. [D-D, Lemme 3] 
The Lie group $L^*$ of invertible 
continuous operators in $E$ is contractible. 
			\end{proposition}
	
\begin{corollary}\cite{bryl:loop}
%4.1.6. Corollary. [D-D, Lemme 4] 
The sheaf $\underline{L}^*_M$ of continuous $L^*$-valued 
functions is soft (cf. \cite{bredon:sheaf})
\end{corollary}
\begin{proposition}\cite{bryl:loop}
%4.1.7. Proposition. 
Let B be a soft sheaf of groups on M. Then 
$H^1\left( M, B\right) = \{1\}$.
\end{proposition}
\begin{proposition}\cite{bryl:loop}
%4.1.8. Proposition. [D-D, Lemme 22] 
Let $\{1 \}\hookto A \hookto B  \onto C \onto \{1\}$ be
a central exact sequence of sheaves of groups over $M$. If $B$ is a soft sheaf, then $\dl_1 : H^1\left(M,C \right) \cong H^2\left(M, A \right)$ is a bijection. 
\end{proposition}
\begin{theorem}\cite{bryl:loop}
%4.1.9. Theorem. 
( Dixmier-Douady) For the Lie group G of algebra 
automorphisms of the Banach algebra K of compact operators on a separable 
Hilbert space E, we have natural bijections
\be 
H^1\left(M, \underline{G}_M \right) \cong H^2\left(M, \underline{\C}^*_M \right)\cong H^3\left(M,\Z\left(1 \right) \right).
\ee
\end{theorem}
\begin{proposition}\cite{bryl:loop}
%4.1.10. Proposition. 
The operation $\otimes$ on $H^1\left(M, \underline{G}_M \right)$ gives   $H^1\left(M, \underline{G}_M \right)$
structure of an Abelian group. The bijection $\dl_1: H^1\left(M, \underline{G}_M \right) \cong H^2\left(M, \underline{\C}^*_M \right)$
is a group isomorphism. 
\end{proposition}
\begin{lemma}\cite{bryl:loop}
%Lemma. 
$H^1\left(M, \underline{G}_M \right)$ is in a natural bijection with the set of isomorphism classes of locally trivial algebra bundles $A\to]M$ with fiber $\K$. 
\end{lemma}
\begin{empt}\label{projective_bundle_empt}\cite{bryl:loop}
For a separable Hilbert space $E$, the {projective space} $\mathbb{P}$ of $E$ is a manifold 
modeled on $E/ \C$. For $\left\{e_n\right\}$ an orthonormal basis of $E$, $E\setminus 0$ is covered by the 
open sets $\sV_j \bydef  = \left\{\left.\sum_{n=1}^\infty x_n e^n\right| x_j \neq 0 \right\}$. $\mathbb{P}$ is covered by the open sets $\sU_j$
The open set $\sV_j$ identifies with the subspace $\left( \C \cdot e_j\right)^\perp$  of $E$; to $v \in \left( \C \cdot e_j\right)^\perp$
corresponds the line spanned by $v + e_j$. Again $p: E\setminus 0 \to  \mathbb{P}$ is  principal 
$C^*$-bundle. 
\end{empt}
\begin{definition}\label{projective_bundle_defn}\cite{bryl:loop}
The {\it projective space 
bundle} is a trivial fiber bundle $p : P \onto M$ with 
fiber the {\it projective space}
$\mathbb{P} \left( E\right) \bydef  (E\setminus \{0\})/\C^*$ of lines in $E$.
\end{definition}
\begin{lemma}\cite{bryl:loop}
%4.1.12. Lemma. 
The group of projective automorphisms of  $\mathbb{P} \left( E\right)$, equipped 
with the topology of uniform convergence on bounded subsets of P(.E), is 
homeomorphic to G. 
\end{lemma}
\begin{proposition}\cite{bryl:loop}
%4.1.13. Proposition. 
There is a natural bijection between the set of iso- 
morphism classes of separable projective space bundles over M and the set 
$H^1(M, \underline{G_M})$ of isomorphism classes of principal $G$-bundles over $M$. 
\end{proposition}
%	\begin{proposition}\label{ctr_lt_prop}\cite{cuntz_meyer_ros:bivariant}
	%Proposition 9.3. 
	%		Let $\H$ be a Hilbert space, and let $\K \bydef \K\left(\H \right)$  be the algebra of		compact operators on $\H$. Then every irreducible *-representation of $\K$ is unitary		equivalent to the standard representation of $\K$ on $\sH$, and every $*$-automorphism		of $\K$ is given by conjugation by a unitary operator on $\H$. The *-automorphism		group of $\K$ can be identified with the topological group $PU\bydef U/\T$ the		projective unitary group of $\H$, with the quotient topology from the strong operator		topology on $U\left(\H\right)$.
	%	\end{proposition}

\begin{proposition}\label{ctr_bundle_prop}\cite{cuntz_meyer_ros:bivariant}
	%Proposition 5.59. 
	%Theorem 9.9 
	(DixmierDouady). 
	Any stable separable algebra $A$ of continuous
	trace over a second-countable locally compact Hausdorff space $\sX$ is isomorphic to
	$\Ga_0\left( \sX, \A\right)$ , the sections vanishing at infinity of a locally trivial bundle of algebras
	over $\sX$, with fibres $\K$ and structure group $\Aut(\K) = PU = U/\T$. Classes of
	such bundles are in natural bijection with the \v{C}ech cohomology group $\check{H}^3\left(\sX, \Z \right)$.
	The 3-cohomology class $\dl\left( A\right)$  attached to (the stabilization of) a continuous-trace
	algebra A is called its DixmierDouady class.
\end{proposition}
\begin{proof}
	Principal $PU$-bundles over $\sU$ are thus classified by
	$\left[\sX, BPU\right] = \left[\sX, K\left( \Z, 3\right) \right] = H^3\left(\sX, \Z \right)$. 
	The details of the proof are presented in \cite{cuntz_meyer_ros:bivariant}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}\label{ctr_d_prop}\cite{cuntz_meyer_ros:bivariant}
	%Proposition 9.11 (P. Green [51,96,104]). 
	Let $\sX$ be a second-countable locally compact
	Hausdorff space, and let $A$ and $B$ be stable algebras of continuous trace over $\sX$.
	Then $A \times_\sX B$ is also a stable continuous-trace algebra over $\sX$, and the DixmierDouady class $\dl \left(A \otimes_\sX B \right)$  of $A \times_\sX B$ is given by $\dl(A) + \dl(B)$. The DixmierDouady class of the opposite algebra $A^{\mathrm{op}}$ is given by $\dl\left( A^{\mathrm{op}}\right)=$ - $\dl\left( A\right)$ , so that
	$A\times_\sX  A^{\mathrm{op}}= C_0\left(\sX, \K\right)$.
\end{proposition}
\begin{proof}
	Here a fragment of the proof is presented.
	From the proposition it follows that that if $A =\Ga_0\left( \sX, \A\right)$ and $B = \Ga_0\left( \sX, \B\right)$, where $\A$ and B are locally trivial bundles of $C^*$-algebras over $\sX$ with fibres isomorphic	to $\K$ then $A\times_\sX B = \Ga_0\left( \sX, \A\otimes B\right)$ where $\A\otimes \B$, where  is the locally trivial bundle with
	fibre $\A_x\widehat \otimes \B_x$ over $x\in \sX$.  It is proven in \ref{ctr_d_prop} that $\dl \left(A \otimes_\sX B \right)= \dl  \left(A  \right)+\left(B \right)$.
	
\end{proof}
\begin{notation}\label{ctr_not}
	If $\sX$ is a locally compact Hausdorff space then we denote by $CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$ the stable
	continuous-trace algebra  with DixmierDouady class $\delta \in \check{H}^3\left(\sX,\Z \right)$. From the Proposition \ref{ctr_d_prop} it follows that
	\be\label{bundle_prod_iso}
	\varphi_{\dl \rho}	:CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\times_\sX CT\left(\sX, \rho \right)\cong CT\left(\sX, \dl +\rho\right).
	\ee
\end{notation}
\begin{proposition}\label{ctr_cup_prop}\cite{cuntz_meyer_ros:bivariant}
	%Proposition 9.17.
	There are natural homomorphisms
	\bea\label{ka_eqn}
	K_\bullet\left( CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right)\otimes_\Z K_\bullet\left( CT\left(\sX, \rho \right)\right) \to K_\bullet\left( CT\left(\sX, \dl + \rho\right)\right),\\
	\label{kx_eqn}
	K_\bullet\left( CT\left(\sX, 0 \right)\right)\cong K^\bullet\left( \sX\right),
	\eea
	where $K_\bullet\left( CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right)$ means $K$-theoretic groups of $C^*$-algebra $ CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$ and $K^\bullet\left( \sX\right)$ means $K$-theoretic groups of the space $\sX$.
\end{proposition}
\subsection{Dixmier Douady theory of groupoids}
\paragraph*{} Here I follow to \cite{bryl:loop}.
Sheaves themselves can be descended. To 
explain this, we start with the more concrete case of principal $G$-bundles, 
for $G$  a Lie group. Say $\sX$ and $\sY$ are smooth manifolds, and $f: \sY \onto \sX$
is a smooth surjective local homeomorphism. Given a principal $G$-bundle 
$\pi: P \to \sX$, setting $Q = P \times_\sX \sY$,we have the pull-back bundle $\pi: Q \to \sY$. 
There is a natural isomorphism $\phi : p^*_1Q\xrightarrow{\cong} p^*_2Q$ the two pull-back bundles 
over $\sY\times_\sX \sY$ , since $fp_1 = fp_2$, which satisfies the following cocycle condition 
\be\label{desc_ppp_eqn}
p^*_{13}\left(\phi \right)= p^*_{23}\left(\phi \right)\circ p^*_{12}\left(\phi \right), 
\ee
an equality of morphisms $p^*_1Q\to p^*_2Q$ of $G$-bundles over the triple fiber 
product $\sY\times_\sX\sY\times_\sX\sY$ . In \eqref{desc_ppp_eqn} $p_1, p_2, p_3 : \sY\times_\sX\sY\times_\sX\sY \to \sY$ are the 
projections on the three factors, and $p_{12},p_{13}p_{23}:\sY\times_\sX\sY\times_\sX\sY 
\to \sY\times_\sX\sY$
are the projections on two of the three factors. 

Conversely, consider a $G$-bundle $\pi : Q\onto \sY$, together with an isomorphism $\phi : p^*_1Q\xrightarrow{\cong} p^*_2Q$ of the two pull-back bundles over $\sY\times_\sX\sY$, which 
satisfies the cocycle condition \eqref{desc_ppp_eqn}. We recover a $G$-bundle $P \onto \sX$, the 
pull-back of which to $\sY$ identifies with $Q\onto \sY$. Indeed we can construct 
the total space $P$ as the quotient space of $Q$ by some equivalence relation 
$\sim$. The relation $\sim$  identifies $q_1$ and $q_2$ if $y_1= \pi\left(q_1 \right)$  and $y_2= \pi\left(q_2 \right)$ satisfy 
$f\left( y_1\right) = f\left( y_2\right)$, and the isomorphism $\phi$ of $G$-bundles over $\sY\times_\sX\sY$, evaluated 
at the point $\left(y_1, y_2 \right)$  of $\sY\times_\sX\sY$ sends $\left( q_1; y_1, y_2\right)$  to $\left( q_2; y_1, y_2\right)$. Condition 
\eqref{desc_ppp_eqn} means precisely that $\sim$ is an equivalence relation. It is then easy to 
see that $P \onto \sX$ is a $G$-bundle; the natural mapping $Q \onto P$ now allows the 
$G$-bundle $Q\onto \sY$ to be identified with the pull-back of $P\onto \sX$ to $\sY$. The 
isomorphism $\phi$ is therefore the natural one between the two inverse images of 
$P$ to $\sY$, so that we have a one-to-one correspondence between the following 
kinds of objects: 
\begin{itemize}
	\item [(i)] a principal $G$-bundle $p: P \onto \sX$; 
\item [(ii)] a principal $G$-bundle $\pi: Q \onto \sY$, together with an isomorphism 
$p^*_1Q \xrightarrow{\cong} p^*_2Q $ of the two pull-back bundles over $\sY \times_\sX \sY$, which satisfies the 	cocycle condition \eqref{desc_ppp_eqn}.
\end{itemize}
The isomorphism $\phi$ in (ii) is called a {\it descent datum} (or {\it descent isomorphism}) for the bundle $Q$ with respect to the mapping $f: \sY \onto \sX$. 
We not only have a one-to-one correspondence between isomorphism 
classes of objects of type (i) and (ii), but we in fact have an equivalence 
of categories. Stated simply, we observe that there exists a category of $G$- 
bundles $p: P\onto \sX$ over $\sX$. The objects are $G$-bundles. A morphism a from 
a $G$-bundle $p_1: P_1 \onto \sX$ to a $G$-bundle  $p_2: P_2 \onto \sX$ is a bundle isomorphism 
$\a : P_1 \cong P_2$ (so $\a$ is a diffeomorphism which commutes with the $G$-actions 
and induces the identity on the base space $\sX$). Note that this category is a 
groupoid, i.e., every morphism between objects is invertible.
 
The second category is associated to the surjective local homeomorphism  $f: \sY \onto \sX$. The objects of this category are pairs $\left(\pi: Q \onto \sY, \phi \right)$  as 
in (ii) above. A morphism from $\left(\pi_1: Q \onto \sY, \phi_1 \right)$ to $\left(\pi_2: Q \onto \sY, \phi_2 \right)$ is 
defined to be an isomorphism $a: Q_1 \cong Q_2$ of $G$-bundles over $\sY$, such that 
the following diagram commutes 
\bean
\begin{tikzcd}
p^*_1Q_1\arrow[r, "p^*_1\a"]\arrow[d, "\phi_1"] & p^*_1Q_2 \arrow[d, "\phi_2"]\\
p^*_2Q_1\arrow[r, "p^*_2\a"] & p^*_2Q_2
\end{tikzcd}
\eean 
This category is also a groupoid. We now obtain 
\begin{proposition}
%5.1.3. Proposition. 
Let $f : \sX \onto \sY$ be a surjective local homeomorphism. 
The pull-back functor $f^*$ induces an equivalence of categories between the 
category of $G$-bundles over $\sX$ and the category of $G$-bundles $G$ over $\sY$, 
equipped with a descent isomorphism $\phi: p^*_1Q \cong p^*_2Q$ satisfying the cocycle 
condition \eqref{desc_ppp_eqn}.
\end{proposition}	
The situation is entirely analogous for sheaves over $\sX$. We have the 
notion of descent datum for a sheaf $\mathscr A$ over $\sY$, namely an isomorphism $\phi: p^{-1}_1 \mathscr A\cong p^{-1}_2 \mathscr A$ of sheaves on $\sY$, which satisfies the analog of \eqref{desc_ppp_eqn} (with the 
pull-backs now denoted by $p^{-1}_{ij}$ rather than $p^*_{ij}$). We define a category of 
such pairs $\left(\mathscr A, \phi \right)$ , and obtain 
\begin{proposition}
%5.1.4. Proposition. 
Let $f: \sY \to \sX$ be a surjective local homeomorphism. 
The inverse image functor $f^{-1}$ induces an equivalence of categories between 
the category of sheaves over $\sX$ and the category of sheaves A over $\sY$, equipped 
with a descent datum $\phi : p^{-1}_1A \cong p^{-1}_2A$ satisfying the cocycle condition \eqref{desc_ppp_eqn}.
\end{proposition}


\section{Miscellany}
	
\begin{remark}\label{polarization_equality_rem}
	For any $C^*$-pre-Hilbert $X$ module, or more  precisely, for any sesquilinear form $\left\langle \cdot , \cdot \right\rangle$ the \textit{polarization equality}
	\be\label{polarization_equality_eqn}
	\begin{split}
		4 \left\langle \xi , \eta \right\rangle=\sum_{k = 0}^3i^k\left\langle \xi + i^k\eta, \xi + i^k\eta \right\rangle
	\end{split}
	\ee 
	is obviously satisfied for all $\xi, \eta \in X$.  If $\H$ is a Hilbert space then there is the following analog of the identity \eqref{polarization_equality_eqn}
	\be\label{polarization_hilb_equality_eqn}
	\\
	\left( \xi , \eta \right)_{\H} = \frac{\sum_{k = 0}^3i^k\left\| \xi + i^k\eta \right\|}{4}, \quad\forall \xi, \eta \in X
	\ee
\end{remark} 
\subsection{Cohomology in algebraic geometry}
\paragraph{} Algebraic geometry operates with Zariski topology (cf. \cite{hartshorne:ag}) However some modifications of the algebraic geometry cab be applied to the considered hare spaces.

\begin{empt}\label{loc_const_triv_empt}
It is proven in \cite{milne:lec} that if $\sX_{\mathfrak{Zariski}}$  is an algebraic manifold with Zariski topology and $\mathscr F$ is a  locally constant sheaf on $\sX_{\mathfrak{Zariski}}$  then
$$
\forall r > 0 \quad H^r\left(\sX_{\mathfrak{Zariski}}, \mathscr F \right) = 0.
$$
\end{empt}
\begin{empt}\cite{hartshorne:ag}
Let A be a noetherian ring, let $S \bydef A\left[x_0, ..., x_n\right]$, and let $\sX \bydef \mathrm{Rroj} S$
be the projective space $\mathbb P^r_A$ over $A$. Let $\mathscr O_\sX\left( 1\right)$  be the twisting sheaf of Serre 
(cf. \cite{hartshorne:ag}). For any sheaf of ($\mathscr O_\sX$ -modules $\mathscr F$, we denote by $\Ga_*\left(\mathscr F \right)$  the graded $S$-module 
$$
\bigoplus_{n \in \Z} \Ga\left(\sX, \mathscr F\left( n\right). \right) 
$$

 \end{empt}
\begin{theorem}\label{projective_ag_coh_thm}\cite{hartshorne:ag}
%Theorem 5.1.
 Let $A$ be a noetherian ring, and let $\sX \bydef \mathbb P^r_A$, with $r \ge 1$. Then: 
 \begin{enumerate}
 	\item[(a)]  the natural map $S \to \Ga_*\left(\mathscr O_\sX \right)  = \sum_{n \in \Z} H^0\left(\sX,\mathscr O_\sX\left( n\right)   \right)$  is an isomorphism of graded $S$-modules; 
 	\item[(b)] $H^i\left( \mathscr O_\sX\left( n\right)\right) = 0$ for $0 < i < r$ and all $n \in \Z$;
 	
 	\item[(c)]	$H^i\left( \mathscr O_\sX\left(-r-1\right)\right)= A$.
 	\item[(d)]	The natural map 
 		$$
 		H^0\left(\sX,O_\sX\left(n\right)  \right) \times 	H^r\left(\sX,O_\sX\left(-n-r-1\right)  \right)\to H^r\left(\sX,O_\sX\left(-r-1\right)  \right)\cong A
 		$$
 			is a perfect pairing of finitely generated free $A$-modules, for each $n \in \Z$. 
 			
 \end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}
\subsection{Fundamental theorem of projective geometry}
\begin{defn}\cite{berger:geometryI}
	Let $\sV. \sV'$ be vector spaces over $K, K'$. a map $f: \sV \to \sV'$ is called {\it semilinear} if there exists an automorphism $\sigma :K \to K'$ such that
	\bean
	f\left(\la x + \mu y \right) = \sigma\left(\la \right) f\left( x\right) + \sigma\left(\mu \right) f\left( y\right) 
	\eean
	for all $x, y\in \sV$, $\la, \mu \in K$. If $\sX, \sX'$ are affine spaces over $K, K'$ a map $f: \sX \to \sX'$ is called {\it semiaffine} if there exists $a \in \sX$ such that $\overline f: \sX_a \to \sX_{f\left(a \right) }$ is semilinear.
	
\end{defn}
\begin{theorem}\cite{berger:geometryI}
Let $\sX$, $\sX'$ be affine spaces of same finite dimension $d \ge 2$. Let $f: \sX \to \sX'$ be a bijection which takes any three collinear points $a, b, c \in \sX'$ into  collinear points $f(a), f(b), f(c)\in \sX'$. Then $f$ is semiaffine
\end{theorem}
\begin{theorem}\label{fund_proj_thm}\cite{berger:geometryI}
Let both $\mathbb{P}\left( E\right)$,   $\mathbb{P}\left( E'\right)$ two projective spaces of equal dimension  $\ge 2$ over fields $K$ and $K'$. Let $f: \mathbb{P}\left( E\right)\cong \mathbb{P}\left( E'\right)$ be a set theoretic bijection such that for any three collinear points $a, b, c \in mathbb{P}\left( E\right)$ the points $f(a), f(b), f(c) \in \mathbb{P}\left( E\right)$ are collinear then there is a semilinear map $f : E \to E'$ with $f = \underline{ \hat f}$
\end{theorem}

\subsection{Cell decomposition of projective spaces}\label{cell_proj_sec}
\paragraph{} Here I follow to \cite{fomenko_fucs_hot}
there the chain of inclusions
\bean
\emptyset = \R P^{-1}\subset \R P^0\subset \R P^1\subset  ... \subset  \R P^n:
\eean
We set $e^q =  \R P^q \setminus \R^{q-1}$ . A characteristic map for $e^q$ may be chosen as the
composition of the canonical projection $D^q \to \R P^q$ and the inclusion
$\R P^q \to \R P^n$. For $n = \infty$, this construction provides a $CW$ decomposition of $\R P^\infty$
with one cell in every dimension.
The construction also has complex, quaternionic, and Cayley analogs. In the
complex case, we get a $CW$ decomposition of $\C P^n$ into $n + 1$ cells $e^0, e^2, e^4, ... , e^{2n} $
and also a $CW$ decomposition of $\C P^\infty$ with one cell of every even dimension.

\end{appendices}

\paragraph{Closed transversals and idempotents of $C^*_r\left(\sV,\F \right)$} 

Let $\left(\sV,\F \right)$ be a foliated manifold, and $N \subset \sV$ a compact submanifold with $\dim N = \codim \F$, everywhere
transverse to the foliation. Then the restriction $\F'$ of $\F$ to a small enough tubular
neighborhood $\sV'$  of $N$ defines on $\sV'$  a fibration with compact base $N$. In other words,
there exists a fibration $\sV' \xrightarrow{p} N$ with fibbers $\R^k$, $k = \dim \F$, such that for any $x \in \sV$
one has $\F_x = \ker\left(p_* \right)_x$. The $C^*$-algebra $C^*_r\left(\sV,\F \right)$ of the restriction of $\sF$ to $\sV'$ is
thus strongly Morita equivalent to $C\left( N\right)$ , and in fact isomorphic to $C\left(N \right)\otimes \K$  where
$\K$ is the $C^*$-algebra of compact operators. In particular it contains an idempotent
$e = e^2 = e^*$, $~e = 1_N \otimes f \in C\left(N \right)\otimes \K$ , where $f$ is a minimal projection in $\K$. Using the
inclusion $C^*_r\left(\sV'.\F' \right) \subset C^*_r\left(\sV,\F \right)$, we thus get an idempotent of $C^*_r\left(\sV,\F \right)$, which we shall now describe more concretely. The transversality of
$N$ to the foliation ensures the existence of a neighborhood $\mathcal W$ of $\G^{(0)}$ in $\G$ such that
\bean
	\ga \in \mathcal W \circ \mathcal W^{-1}, \quad s\left(\ga  \right) \in N \quad r\left(\ga  \right) \in N\quad \Rightarrow \quad \ga \in \G^{(0)},
\eean
where $\G^{(0)}\bydef \left\{\left(x,x \right) | x \in \sV\right\}$ is the set of units of $\G$ . Let then $\xi$ be a smooth
section on the submanifold $r^{-1} \left( N\right)\subset \G$ of the bundle $s^*\left( \Om^{1/2}\right)$  of half-densities, $\xi \in \Coo_c\left(r^{-1} \left( N\right), s^*\left( \Om^{1/2}\right) \right) $, such that
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item[($\a$)] $\supp \xi \in \mathcal W$
			\item[($\bt$)] $\int_{r\left( \ga\right)= y  }\left|\xi\left( \ga\right)  \right|^2=1\quad \forall y \in N $.
		\end{enumerate}
The equality 
$$
e \left(\ga \right) = \sum_{\substack{s\left(\ga'\right) = s\left( ga\right) \\ r\left(\ga' \right)\in N }}\overline \xi\left(\ga' \ga^{-1} \right)\xi\left( \ga'\right)  
$$
 defines an idempotent
$$
e \in \Coo_c\left( \G, \Om^{1/2}\right) \subset C^*_r\left(\sV,\F \right).
$$
Indeed, for each $x \in \sV$ the operator $\pi_x\left(e \right)$  in $L^2\left( \G_x\right)$  is the orthogonal projection on
the closed subspace of $L^2\left( \G_x\right)$ spanned by a set of orthogonal vectors labeled by the
countable set $I \bydef r^{-1}(N) \cap \G_x$, namely $\left\{\eta_\ga\right\}_{\ga\in I}$ , where
$$
\eta_\ga\left( \ga'\right) = \xi\left(\ga\left( \ga'\right)^{-1}  \right) 
$$
A more canonical way to dene the (equivalence class of the) above idempotent $e \in \Coo_c\left(r^{-1} \left( N\right), s^*\left( \Om^{1/2}\right) \right) $
 is to show that the $C^*$-module $eA$, $A\bydef C^*_r\left(\sV,\F \right)$, is the same as the completion of $\Coo_c\left(r^{-1} \left( N\right), s^*\left( \Om^{1/2}\right) \right)$ 
with the right action $\Coo_c\left(\G,  \Om^{1/2} \right)$ given by convolution, for f $$
\left(\xi * f \right)\left( \ga \right) \bydef \int_{\ga_1 \circ \ga_2=\ga}\xi\left( \ga_1\right) f\left( \ga_2\right) \quad \forall \xi \in \Coo_c\left(r^{-1} \left( N\right), s^*\left( \Om^{1/2}\right) \right).
$$
and with the $\Coo_c\left( \G, \Om^{1/2}\right) $-valued inner product given by
$$
\left\langle\xi, \eta \right\rangle \bydef \sum_{\substack{s\left(\ga'\right) = s\left( ga\right) \\ r\left(\ga' \right)\in N }}\overline \xi\left(\ga' \ga^{-1} \right)\eta\left( \ga'\right), \quad \forall  \xi, 
\eta \in \Coo_c\left(r^{-1} \left( N\right), s^*\left( \Om^{1/2}\right) \right).
$$
The construction of this $C^*$-module $\E_N$ over $C^*_r\left(\sV,\F \right)$ makes sense whether $N$ is compact or not, but in the former case the identity is a compact endomorphism of $\E_N$ and $\E_N \bydef eC^*_r\left(\sV,\F \right)$ for a suitable idempotent $e \in C^*_r\left(\sV,\F \right)$ (the identity being of rank
one). 


If $N$ is compact and meets every leaf of $ C^*_r\left(\sV,\F \right)$, then $\E_N$ gives a strong Morita equivalence between $C^*_r\left(\sV,\F \right)$ and the $C^*$-algebra of compact endomorphisms of $\E_N$ which, if
we assume that $N$ is compact, is {\it unital}. This $C^*$-algebra is the convolution $C^*$-algebra
of the reduced groupoid $\G_N$:
$$
\G_N\left\{\ga \in \G \left| r\left(\ga \right) \in N, \quad s\left(\ga \right) \in N \right.\right\}
$$
The groupoid $\G_N$ is a manifold of dimension $q= \codim \F$, and the convolution product
in $\Coo_c\left( \G_N\right)$  is given by
\be
\begin{split}
\left( f*g\right)\left( \ga\right)  = \sum_{\ga_1\circ \ga_2=\ga}f\left(\ga_1 \right) g\left(\ga_2 \right)\\
f^*\left(\ga \right) = \overline{f\left( \ga^{-1}\right) }.
\end{split}
\ee
\section{CUT}

\begin{remark}
	Any open subset of $\sU_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}} \subset \mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}$ equals to
	\be\label{open_g_eqn}
	\sU_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}} = \mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}\setminus \bigcap_{j= 0}^n V_j
	\ee
	where $V_1, ..., V_n \subset 
	\mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)$ are linear subspaces. \end{remark}
\begin{remark}\label{compact_nonempt_rem}
	If both $\sU_1, \sU_2 \subset \mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}$ are nonempty open subsets then from \eqref{open_g_eqn} it follows that $\sU_1 \cap \sU_2 \neq \emptyset$. Similar result has the algebraic geometry, i.e. intersection  of two nonempty,  open with respect to Zariski topology sets is not empty (cf. \cite{hartshorne:ag}).
\end{remark}
!!!!!


\begin{empt}
If  $\dim \H = \infty$ and $\left\{L_0, L_1, ...\right\}$ is a set of mutually orthogonal codimension one projective subspaces of $\mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)$ then
$$
\mathbb{P}\left( \H\right) = \bigcup_{j=0}^\infty \left( \mathbb{P}\left(\H \right) \setminus L_j\right) 
$$
Similarly 
$$
\mathbb{P}\left( \C^n\right) = \bigcup_{j=0}^{n} \left( \mathbb{P}\left( \C^n\right) \setminus L_j\right). 
$$
where $\left\{L_0,  ..., L_n\right\}$ is a set of mutually orthogonal codimension one projective subspaces of $\mathbb{P}\left( \C^n\right)$.
If 
\be\label{comp_cov_eqn}
\mathscr W\bydef \left\{ \mathbb{P}\left(\H \right) \setminus L_j\right\}_{j = 0, 1, ... } \quad \text{or} \quad \mathscr W\bydef \left\{ \mathbb{P}\left( \C^n\right)\setminus L_j\right\}_{j = 0,..., n }
\ee then
\be\label{cp_nerve_eqn}
\begin{split}
	\forall \sigma \in K\left(\mathscr W\right)\quad \sU_{\sigma} = \sH \setminus \bigcup_{j = 0}^{n_\sigma} L^\sigma_j,\\
	\forall j = 1,..., n \quad L^\sigma_j \text{ is a linear subspace of the Hilbert space } \sH \quad \codim_{\R} ~ L^\sigma_j  \ge 2,
\end{split}
\ee
where the inclusion $\sU_{\sigma} = \sH \setminus \bigcup_{j = 0}^{n_\sigma} L^\sigma_j$ follows from the Definition \ref{projective_bundle_defn};
From the equation \eqref{cp_nerve_eqn} it follows that 
\be\label{nerve_0_eqn}
\begin{split}
	\mathfrak{Lattice}\left(\sU_{\sigma} \right) \cong \mathfrak{Lattice}\left(\H' \right),\\
	\forall p > 0 \quad \forall \sigma \in K\left(\mathscr W\right) \quad H^p\left( \sU_{\sigma};\mathscr A \right)= 0.
\end{split}
\ee
where $\sH'$ is a Hilbert space and the isomorphism of semi-lattices comes from the inclusion 
$\sU_{\sigma}\subset \sH'$.
If  $F$ is an Abelian group and  $\overline F$ is  $F$-locally constant sheaf  (cf, Definition \ref{constant_presheaf_defn}) on $\mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)_{\mathfrak{Hausdorff}}$ (cf, Definition  and $\mathscr W= \left\{ \mathbb{P}\left(\H \right) \setminus L_j\right\}_{j = 0, 1, ... }$ or  $\mathscr W= \left\{ \mathbb{P}\left( \C^n\right)\setminus L_j\right\}_{j = 0,..., n }$ then 
$H^p\left( \sU_{\sigma};\mathscr A \right)= 0$  for $p > 0$ and
all $\sigma \in K\left(\mathscr W\right)$ where  $K\left(\mathscr W\right)$ is the nerve of $\mathscr W$ (cf. Definition \ref{nerve_defn}). 
\end{empt}
\begin{lemma}\label{trivial_cech_lem}
If  $\sX \to \sY$ is a bijective continuous map and $F$ is an Abelian group then
\be
\forall p > 0 \quad H^p\left(\sX, F  \right) = 0 \quad \Rightarrow \quad H^p\left(\sY, F  \right) = 0
\ee
where the notation \eqref{locally_const_not_eqn} for locally constant sheaves is used.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
Clearly the singleton covering $\left\{\sX\right\}$ of $\sX$ satisfies to the hypothesis of the Theorem \ref{top_nerve_thm}. Any covering $\mathscr U \bydef \left\{
\sU_\iota \right\}_{\iota \in  I}$ of $\sY$ is a covering of $\sX$. For any class $\left[c_\sY\right] \in \check  H^p\left(\sY, F  \right)$ there is a covering $\mathscr U$ such that $\left[c_\sY\right]$ is represented by the cycle 
\bean
c_\sY =	\sum_{j = 1} ^n\a^j_{\iota_0,...,\iota_{p}}\in \check C^p\left( \mathscr U, F\right).
\eean
This cycle can be regarded as the cycle in $ c_\sX\in \check C^p\left( \mathscr U, F\right)$. From the Theorem \ref{top_nerve_thm} it turns out that $\left[c_\sX\right]$ can be represented by the chain
\bean
\begin{split}
	c'_\sX = \sum_{j = 0}^n	\left( \tau^r \a_{j_0,..., j_{n}} \right)\in \check C^p\left( \left\{\sX\right\}, F\right).
\end{split}
\eean
(cf. \eqref{tau_c_eqn}) where $\tau : \mathscr U \to \left\{\sX\right\}$ is the unique map onto the singleton covering (cf. \eqref{cech_tau_eqn}). It turns out that $\left[c_\sY\right]$ can be represented by the cycle
\bean
c'_\sY = \sum_{j = 0}^n	\left( \tau^r \a_{j_0,..., j_{n}} \right)\in \check C^p\left( \left\{\sY\right\}, F\right)
\eean  
From $\left[c'_\sX\right]= 0\in \check H^p\left(\sX, F  \right)$ it follows that there is $b_\sX \in \check C^p\left( \left\{\sX\right\}, F\right)$ such that $c'_\sX = d_{p -1}b_\sX$. The chain $b_\sX$ uniquely yields the chain $b_\sY \in \check C^p\left( \left\{\sY\right\}, F\right)$ with $c'_\sY = d_{p -1}b_\sY$. It turns out that $\left[c'_\sY\right]= \left[c_\sY\right]= 0$. So one has $\check H^p\left(\sY, F  \right)=H^p\left(\sY, F  \right) = 0$.
\end{proof}
\begin{theorem}\label{compact_thm}
For any Abelian group $F$ the map $\phi_{\H} : \mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)_{\mathfrak{Hausdorff}}\to \mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}$ yields  the natural isomorphism
$$
H^*\left( \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\K\left(\H \right), F\right)  \right)\cong H^*\left(\mathbb{P}\left(\H \right) _{\mathfrak{Gelfand}},  F \right) \cong H^*\left(\mathbb{P}\left(\H \right) _{\mathfrak{Hausdorff}},  F\right)
$$
where the notation \eqref{locally_const_not_eqn} for locally constant sheaves is used.

\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
If $\mathscr W$ is given by \eqref{cp_nerve_eqn} then from the equation \eqref{nerve_0_eqn} and the Theorem \ref{top_nerve_thm} it follows that
$$
H^*\left(\mathbb{P}\left( \C^n\right)_{\mathfrak{Hausdorff}},  F \right) \cong \check H^*\left( \mathscr W;  F\right).
$$

Taking into account that $\mathbb{P}\left( \C^n\right) \setminus L_j$ is open in $\mathbb{P}\left(\H \right)_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}$ for any $j$ one has
\be\label{proj_h_eqn}
H^*\left(\mathbb{P}\left(\H \right) _{\mathfrak{Gelfand}},  F \right) \cong H^*\left(\mathbb{P}\left(\H \right) _{\mathfrak{Hausdorff}},  F\right)
\ee
\end{proof}
